I have windows 2000 and set it up without any problem on default. My IP set
on default "*". Did not encouter any errors at all. Your question was quite
vauge. Were you able to get up the web based interface? or does site show up
via local host? What I found out was that my ISP blocked port 80 the hard
way. I uninstalled everything including firewalls and stuff and still didn't
work. But found out it was my damn ISP blocked port 80. I changed the port
setting to different port and it worked fine. Heres a cool too to check what
port your ISP blocks www.portdetective.com if that is the problem. Good
luck.

Dear Craig,

Saturday, December 01, 2001, 10:27:03 AM, you wrote:

>> Do any xitami-log-examening tools exist?

> http://www.statslab.cam.ac.uk/~sret1/analog/

looks extremely good, but analog quircks about the logformat?

What I did now was edit analog.cfg and tell analog where my logfiles
are and what the output should be:
==
LOGFILE \\server\c\xitami\logs\ac*.*
OUTFILE \\server\c\inetpub\wwwroot\analogreport.html
==

This seems to work. That is, analog tries processing the log-files.

But analog tells me:
==
  logfile \\server\c\xitami\logs\ac011122.log: turn debugging on or try
  different LOGFORMAT
    Current logfile format:
      %S %j %j [%d/%M/%Y:%h:%n:%j] "%j%w%r%wHTTP%j" %c %b "%f" "%B"\n
      %S %j %j [%d/%M/%Y:%h:%n:%j] "%j%w%r" %c %b "%f" "%B"\n
      %S %j %j [%d/%M/%Y:%h:%n:%j] "%r" %c %b "%f" "%B"\n
===

But I have difficulty entering the right format. This is what the
lines look like in my access.log files:

===
213.84.56.202 - - [17/Nov/2001:00:07:28 +0100] "GET /sandston.gif
HTTP/1.1"   200   9706  "http://hace.dyndns.org/diplomacy/dipned.html"
"Mozilla/4.0 (compatible; MSIE 6.0; Windows 98)"
===

(this is one entry from the logfile, all on one line)

If you know the right (xitami) LOGFORMAT I should enter for the above
logfile-line I would be very much helped!

[ Later ]

It seems analog did something after all!
Have a look at the results at:
http://hace.dyndns.org/analogreport.html

But then again: How should I disable all the '/script/' logging?
It does not recognize the '404' message, see the following line:

===
62.194.210.43     -     -     [17/Nov/2001:15:27:17     +0100]    "GET
/scripts/..%252f../winnt/system32/cmd.exe?/c+dir  HTTP/1.0"  404 -1 ""
""
===

Thanks in advance,

hello !

i'm using xitami for some months now. i started writing cgi with visual 
basic and it works perfectly (with no knowledge of programming in VB --long 
ago i did some programming in cobol and fortran). Xitami even parses the 
form fields so i don't have to do it myself! (i tried the well-known 
win-cgi.bas but the object code was some 120 kB, but when using only the 
needed statements the object code is only 15..25k)
i'm even writing a complete order administration (written _years_ ago and 
ported from quickbasic).  It can search through 12000 records, send e-mail 
and faxes and generate output in less than a second.

But there is nobody posting messages about VB cgi (indeed it works very 
well so you expect no reclamations and questions). Are some people out 
there also working with VB5.0? (maybe we could start an other mailing list 
so we don't disturb those using PHP...)
I have only one single question, but till now didn't find any answer: can't 
get any file download done. When checking the files on the server just 
after a download i don't find any file that contains anything that was 
downloaded.

You can mail me directly <marc@verfaillie.com>


Thanks,

marc

this..

This is not the forum for trying to convert someone from operating system to
another.

The original poster was asking for help for a particular situation. Your
response provided no help for his query. Suggesting that he switch to another
operating system was a fruitless effort.

While I can understand your enthusiasm for *nix based platforms, this is not
the place for it. If you can't offer meaningful help in regards to the context
of the questions asked, please refrain from posting. Doing otherwise serves no
purpose other than to drive those who are honestly looking for a helping hand
else where.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Dec  2 08:09:20 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Sun, 02 Dec 2001 03:09:20 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] somebody using visual basic out there?
References: <5.0.2.1.2.20011201165821.01c22d00@190.190.190.1>
Message-ID: <3C09E1B0.669585CA@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  i started writing cgi with visual basic

I would have expected you to get razzed on that point: "You
program in BASIC? Yuck!", rather than the non-unix point. Even
FORTRAN gets more respect than BASIC. 

I'd argue that *nix is NOT universally "more stable"... but this
isn't the place. 

Using MS Basic "prevents" you from porting to non-MS platforms,
which isn't much of an issue for me. I have stable MS machines.
If I had to move to a commercial hosting site, most assume unix
but plenty of NT hosts are available. 

Yes, I too program in BASIC, when nobody is watching. I have a VB
filter serving many pages on my site from a database. And because
I am a really crude guy, I also have a QuickBasic 4.5 (1985 DOS
tool) CGI handling forms. Hey: it works, I understand it; what
more could I want? 

>From one Basic-user to another: once you get over Perl's chaos,
it ain't as bad as it looks. I have 21 years experience in BASIC,
I spent a month part-time writing my VB filter. After a month of
poking at Perl trying to get a handle on it, I did more in one
day than I did in a month with VB. Some things are still better
in VB-- nobody's string functions compare with MS BASIC. But many
things web-related are pre-made in Perl. 

>  the object code was some 120 kB, but when using only the 
needed statements the object code is only 15..25k

One think I learned in years of QB programming, and the same is
true in VB: the object code size is meaningless. The compiler is
pretty sloppy. Much of that "excess" code won't be used. And even
more so in VB, where ANY program loads and initializes a 2 Meg
library, which dwarfs the code you or I will write. (Perl does
the same thing, only differently.) If your code reads better with
(or without) some function or module, do it regardless of how big
the BIN or EXE file comes out. 

>  It can search through 12000 records, send e-mail and faxes and generate output in less than a second.

My VB filter does a very dumb sequential search on a flat text
file and can pull 1,000 hits in less than a second on P-350. Some
things in VB are slow (case-sensitive text match) but most things
are bound by disk and network speed, not program speed. A rough
comparison with old QB45 (which ran well on 8088-5 machines)
shows little difference. 

Your question may be about VB but it probably is really about CGI
or Xitami's interface to CGI, which IS on-point on this list. 

>  can't get any file download done. When checking the files on the server just after a download i don't find any file 

Without details of what you mean "download" I can't begin to
think where to look. Do you really mean "upload"? What HTML code
do you use in the form? Does your VB code believe it has handled
a file? 

> Xitami even parses the form fields so i don't have to do it myself!

Yes, but MultiPartEncoded is a bit tricky. 

This is one place where I'd be inclined to use Perl. BASIC/VB's
notion of STDIN and STDOUT is a bit arcane... well to be frank,
it isn't like unix and CGI assumes that kind of input stream.
Perl has modules, or you can find pre-made File UpLoad Perl
scripts. Since form-upload really does not have to interface
directly with your VB code, it should not interfere. 

And BTW: I would have written that VB filter in QB; in fact I
prototyped it in QB. The thing that "forced" me to VB is QB45's
64K limit on string-space. I could have worked-around, but I was
attracted to the "infinite" heap in VB-Win. 

 -PRR

I have cable-modem access here in the Netherlands.

Before August, the provider was the Finnish Telecom company 'Sonera'.
We had no possibility for running servers because they locked out all
incoming requests on ports 1-1024 (apart from certain necessary secure
ports or something). It was 79 Guilders (EUR 36) a month.

Currently Sonera has sold the Cable over here to UPC, so now I have
Chello (see www.chello.nl) for 99 Guilders (EUR 45) a month and can
run a HTTP server (yes!).

Hello from Belgium

Thank you all for your replies (to the list and to me personally).
I will definitely try power basic from powerbasic.com (the console version) 
since i don't need an interface when sending html output to another 
computer. _visual_ basic is too much for me.


I will define my problem more specifically:
The company i work for has an internet printer (Remote Internet Printing). 
It reads it's mail via pop-3 like an ordinary mail client and prints it 
out. It works perfectly for text documents.

The printer can also print postscript files, but it can't handle mime. A 
postcript file attached to a message is mime-encoded, but the printer can't 
decode it (and there is no upgrade). Printing postcript to the LAN printer 
is OK (windows file and printer sharing).


So i want to get the postcript file from the remote user using http
Once the file is on the server computer i can do anything to adapt the 
message to the printer standards and send it without mime to the printer 
mailbox.

I tried following html to send a sample file
<html><body>

    <form ACTION="/cgi-bin/env.exe" method="POST">
       <input type=file name="123.txt"><br>
       <input type=submit value="Send">
    </form>

</body></html>

env.exe simply sends the environment and other input files back to the browser.

What i get on the server is the name of the file, but not the content itself!
Is there something wrong with the html (i don't think so)?

That's what the back-end program receives from Xitami (the environment).
CGI_STDERR=cgierr.log
CGI_STDOUT=C:\WINDOWS\TEMP\pipe0353.cgo
CGI_STDIN=C:\WINDOWS\TEMP\pipe0353.cgi
QUERY_STRING=123.txt=C%3A%5Clog.txt
CGI_URL=/cgi-bin
CGI_ROOT=C:\XITAMI\cgi-bin
DOCUMENT_ROOT=\\src\public\marc\uploads
PATH_TRANSLATED=\\src\public\marc\uploads
PATH_INFO=
REMOTE_ADDR=217.136.228.83
REMOTE_HOST=217.136.228.83
REMOTE_USER=-
CONTENT_LENGTH=22
CONTENT_TYPE=application/x-www-form-urlencoded
SCRIPT_NAME=\cgi-bin\env.exe
SCRIPT_PATH=cgi-bin
REQUEST_METHOD=POST
GATEWAY_INTERFACE=CGI/1.1
SERVER_PROTOCOL=HTTP/1.0
SERVER_PORT=80
SERVER_URL=http://web.verfaillie.com/
SERVER_NAME=web.verfaillie.com
SERVER_VERSION=2.4d6
SERVER_SOFTWARE=Xitami
FORM_123_TXT=C:\log.txt


The following line is the content of the CGI_STDIN file:
123.txt=C%3A%5Clog.txt


It's actually the same as the QUERY_STRING
Where can i find the file that (probably?) was send by the browser?

I don't know if the problem is html-related (wrong coding of html), 
xitami-related (some incorrect configuration) or visual basic related 
(can't get all the data from xitami)


Thank you very much !


Marc

> Virusdefinities dagelijks aangepast.
> De postmaster,
>
You need to have a form with ENCTYPE set i.e.
<form ACTION="/cgi-bin/env.exe" method="POST" 
enctype=|"multipart/form-data"| >


Francis

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Dec  2 19:22:26 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Sun, 02 Dec 2001 14:22:26 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami and basic
References: <5.0.2.1.2.20011202115044.01c17840@190.190.190.1>
Message-ID: <3C0A7F72.EA13EBBF@rci.rutgers.edu>

>  power basic from powerbasic.com 

An interesting product. Amazing that he has kept it going for 2 decades
against Mighty MicroSoft. 

>  an internet printer... It reads its mail via pop-3 like an ordinary mail client and prints it out. 

An interesting way to print. I have printers where if you do an FTP STOR
to them, they "store" the file as ink on paper. 

Never heard of one with an email interface, but that would be convenient
for many people. 

Is the printer itself getting mail from the POP mailbox, or are you
using a DOS/Win machine to get mail and give it to the printer? 

>  can also print postscript files, 

OK, it is a PS printer that can auto-switch from text to PostScript. 

> but it can't handle mime. 

Ah. If you are using a PC to get mail and send it to the printer, there
are standalone command-line MIME decoders. Most are very smart: you can
send them plain un-MIME text and they will give it back unchanged. One
old favorite is UUDECODE.

So after you get email from the POP server and put it in a file, use
SHELL to pass the file through a decoder

 Folder$ = "C:\spool\mail\"
 MessageNumber$ = "1234"
 InFile$ = MessageNumber$ + ".bin"
 OutFile$ = MessageNumber$ + ".txt"
 SHELL "command /c UUDECODE <" + Infile$ + " >" + Outfile$
 SHELL "command /c copy " + OutFile$ + " PRN"



 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Dec  4 00:44:44 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 04 Dec 2001 13:44:44 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] password encryption
In-Reply-To: Message from "Peter" <peter@iwebsl.com>
 of "Mon, 03 Dec 2001 19:26:08 CDT." <004c01c17c5a$45d08980$205dddd8@LACKY>
Message-ID: <200112040044.NAA28390@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <004c01c17c5a$45d08980$205dddd8@LACKY>, "Peter" writes:
>Hello
>I have a quick question for you that I don't see in the docs anywhere.
>Can you use any other type of password file/type encryption with this server

Not at present, no.  Xitami only supports its niave plain text password
files.

At some stage, probably the same point that it supports encrypted
passwords, it will add support for other authentication formats, maybe
by using PAM where that is available.

Contributions of code to do this welcomed :-)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Dec  4 01:22:11 2001

Hello thanks for the quick response. I'm pretty surprised that no encryption
is used when they are publicly available for use. Perl offers a MD5 mod I
believe that php uses a similar method. PAM I'm not fimilair with. Below is
a bit of perl to encrypt a password (MD5 mod need s to be installed)

use Digest::MD5 qw/md5_hex/;
$enc_pass=md5_hex($password);

Peter

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Dec  4 14:45:25 2001

Michael Pierce wrote:

>Hello,
>   In my directory listing template "myhttpdir.gsl" I would like to run have
>a server side
>that runs a ".exe" on each file with a certain extension. The following
>code:
>.    if defined (type)
>.       if type = "lnk"
>.           <!-- #include virtual="/cgi-bin/resolvelnk.exe" -->
>.       endif
>.endif
>
>Does not run the "resolvelnk" executable.
>.           <!-- #include virtual="/cgi-bin/resolvelnk.exe" -->
>
This line does not do what you want it to do.
.           <!-- #include virtual="/cgi-bin/resolvelnk.exe" -->

Firstly it should give an error because <!-- is not a recognised gsl command 

Then if you were to remove the leading . it might at least give a page 
with the cgi-bin line in it but I don't think it would execute it as it 
would be treated as a static html page not a dynamic shtml one.

What you need to do - which is tricky - is to use commands like .literal 
or .xml to load the text and the mangle it but I'm not sure you can do 
what you would want to do (assign a variable to the file contents which 
you would then manipulate with substr)...

Francis

Open a Command Prompt and try this:

telnet localhost 80 <enter>
GET / <enter>
<enter>


	Does telnet connect to the web server port ? Does the GET fetch the
document back ? Is  it the Xitami page you expect ?

	I've seen people try to install Xitami on a Win2k machine which already had
an IIS server running on port 80. Obviously that fails.

	What exactly are you trying to do ? Force Xitami to bind to only 1
interface, therefore exposing the web server only to that LAN ?

	Also, try a real message subject next time.

marcio

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Dec  4 20:27:56 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 05 Dec 2001 09:27:56 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami with Linux
In-Reply-To: Message from Francis Turner <francis.turner@freesbee.fr>
 of "Tue, 04 Dec 2001 16:55:37 BST." <3C0CF1F9.4040101@freesbee.fr>
Message-ID: <200112042027.JAA03602@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3C0CF1F9.4040101@freesbee.fr>, Francis Turner writes:
>Does gcc -DDEBUG make a performance difference to Xitami?

-DDEBUG enables the assertions in the code which check that things are
"as expected" when it is running.  (The assertion should never failure,
they're doublechecks that the program logic is correct.)

There will be a small perfomance overhead, but I wouldn't expect it to
make much of a difference except perhaps if your server is using every
last bit of CPU time, and begging for more.

Yes, -DDEBUG is enabled by default.  You can disable it you setting the
production build model, with: CCPRODLEVEL=production.  (That will also
strip the debugging symbols off the binary.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Dec  5 14:33:37 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)
Date: Wed, 5 Dec 2001 09:33:37 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] xitami for linux and php
In-Reply-To: <4342.202.58.96.38.1007553428.squirrel@webmail.pilnet.com>
Message-ID: <001101c17d99$d36d0490$0201a8c0@celeron2k>

To enable PHP , add this to the end of xitami's defaults.cfg 

[Filter]
php=path/to/php/executable

[Mime] 
.php=application/x-httpd-php3 

Restart the server 


marcio

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Dec  5 16:45:57 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Johnson, Nathan J)
Date: Wed, 05 Dec 2001 11:45:57 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] (no subject)
Message-ID: <9EFD49E2FB59D411AABA0008C7E675C005FB6C07@emss04m10.ems.lmco.com>

Just another idea, is TCP/IP installed on the machine?  With no TCP/IP stack
running, even local loopback won't work. 
Make sure that in the network setup for Win2000 has the TCP/IP protocol
installed.  I can't imagine it wouldn't unless the machine isn't networked
at all.

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Peter)

Subject: [Xitami] (no subject)
References: <NEBBIJCGMNPMOJGCJHMGAEBEDCAA.xitami@image602.com> <00ac01c17c8a$363971f0$0ddcf4d0@dds.davidge.com> <001b01c17d2d$528e6ab0$205dddd8@LACKY> <005001c17d42$84403b00$0ddcf4d0@dds.davidge.com>
Message-ID: <001301c17daf$47cd24e0$205dddd8@LACKY>

Your browser address field, start your browser and type in http://127.0.0.1
or local host. If you don't have local loopback go to your windows directory
and looks for a file called hosts there will also be host.sam forget about
that one. In the host file make sure you have this entry.

127.0.0.1       localhost

You should also check to make sure you have TCP/IP installed in your
networking.

Peter

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Dec  5 19:48:10 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 06 Dec 2001 08:48:10 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] (no subject)
In-Reply-To: Message from "Erik A." <erik@davidge.com>
 of "Wed, 05 Dec 2001 00:28:25 CDT." <002d01c17d4d$a9d66b40$0ddcf4d0@dds.davidge.com>
Message-ID: <200112051948.IAA13323@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <002d01c17d4d$a9d66b40$0ddcf4d0@dds.davidge.com>, "Erik A." writes:
>My TCP/IP is installed on the machine, but i keep getting that message that
>says:
>Could not open HTTP port 80-Port is already used by another server
>(WSAEADDRINUSE).

In that case there is probably another HTTP server running -- perhaps
IIS if you are using Windows.  (All sorts of things install bits of IIS
because they think you need it :-( )

>From a shell prompt do:

netstat -na

and look for a "...:80...... LISTEN" line; if you see one (before
starting Xitami) then you've definitely got another webserver running.
In which case look at the task list for likely suspects.

If you don't want to stop the other server, you can run Xitmai on 
another port with:

xitami -b BASE

where base is the number to _offset_ all the Xitami ports by, eg:

xitami -b 5000

makes the HTTP port 5080, so you need to use URLs like:

http://localhost:5080/....

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

>
> In that case there is probably another HTTP server running -- perhaps
> IIS if you are using Windows.  (All sorts of things install bits of IIS
> because they think you need it :-( )
>
> >From a shell prompt do:
>
> netstat -na
>
> and look for a "...:80...... LISTEN" line; if you see one (before
> starting Xitami) then you've definitely got another webserver running.
> In which case look at the task list for likely suspects.
>
> If you don't want to stop the other server, you can run Xitmai on
> another port with:
>
> xitami -b BASE
>
> where base is the number to _offset_ all the Xitami ports by, eg:
>
> xitami -b 5000
>
> makes the HTTP port 5080, so you need to use URLs like:
>
> http://localhost:5080/....
>
> Ewen
>
> --
> Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com
>
> --
> Xitami Users Mailing List -- For Xitami support
> To unsubscribe: http://lists.xitami.org/mailman/listinfo/xitami
>

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Dec  5 22:19:24 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)
Date: Wed, 5 Dec 2001 17:19:24 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] (no subject)
In-Reply-To: <000f01c17d6f$d960dbd0$0ddcf4d0@dds.davidge.com>
Message-ID: <005801c17dda$e56ea220$0201a8c0@celeron2k>

	Mistery then. Nothing running (can't telnet, netstat does not show
anything) and yet you are told the port is not available because something
is running already ? Are you sure ?Weird.

	Any chance you are installing from a non-administrator account and Windows
NT/2000 will not allow access to a privileged port ? (< 1024) I know UNIX
systems have that, so that's why I ask.

	BTW, Port 81 you are seeing in your netstat is is for Xitami's LRWP
protocol. That's why I think the theory above is not valid, otherwise it
would not install on port 81 either.

	Which Xitami are you running ? As a service or the one with the little GUI
on the taskbar (lower right corner) ? If as a service, what happens when you
run this from the console:

		net start xitami


	BTW, if you want to be able to tell which apps are running in these ports,
use http://www.atelierweb.com/pscan/ "AWPS - Atelier Web Port Scanner" (menu
Utilities->Enhanced Ports Finder)


marcio

1) use the web interface as I said, don't play with individual files
2) follow the links as I said, you will end up in the SSI config screen. you
will click on "Configuration" on the 1st screen, and then on SSI on the 2nd
screen (text toolbar at the top)

The impression I get from your message is that you did not get to the SSI
screen in your web browser.

marcio

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Dec  6 03:56:32 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)
Date: Wed, 5 Dec 2001 22:56:32 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] #exec
In-Reply-To: <021601c17e03$33631e20$05fea8c0@jjb>
Message-ID: <000201c17e09$fdc4e7b0$0100a8c0@celeron2k>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_0003_01C17DE0.14F1ECF0
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit

Interesting... Mine reads like this:

      Aliases Errors SSI MIMEs WSX Filters DDNS Advanced  Server Vhosts CGI
Security Logging FTP



The same screen says I have Xitami v2.5b1 even though I downloaded the b4.

You shouild tweak c:\xitami\defaults.cfg, based on c:\xitami\xitami.cfg.
Don't change c:\xitami\xitami.cfg

This is what I have in mine, for example:


[Cgi]
    Dirlist = "1"
    Form-query = "1"

[Filter]
    .php = "c:\\php\\php.exe"
    .php3 = "c:\\php\\php.exe"
    .pl = "c:\\perl\\bin\\perl.exe"

[Mime]
.php=application/x-httpd-php
.php3=application/x-httpd-php3
.pl=application/x-httpd-perl


[Ftp]
    Enabled = "0"

[Security]
    Filename = "defaults.aut"

[Server]
    Autostart = "1"
    Priority = "2"
    Recover = "1"

[Win32]
    16bit-cgi = "1"


    And this is what you can override in it about SSI: (note the exec=0 by
default)


#   ------------------------------------------------------------------------
-
#   SSI configuration section
#
#   This section controls Xitami's built-in server-side includes (SSI)
#   handling.

[Ssi]
#   Lets you enable/disable SSI handling.

    enabled=1

#   Specifies the format for times shown by SSI pages.

    timefmt=%A, %d-%b-%y %H:%M:%S %Z

#   Specifies whether size should be shown as bytes or as
#   abbreviations (Kb, Mg). Anything other than the string "bytes" is
#   taken to mean that sizes are shown as abbreviations.

    sizefmt=bytes

#   The timeout for CGI programs called from the SSI agent.

    timeout=30

#   Error message shown when an SSI command fails. The %s symbol is
#   replaced by the cause of the problem.

    errmsg=<p>[xitami SSI: %s]

#   If 1, allows CGIs to be executed using the #exec command. Since
#   this is a security weakness, this option is switched-off by
#   default.

    exec=0


marcio

Subject: [Xitami] #exec

------=_NextPart_000_0020_01C17E34.A574A9D0
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

Hi!
Surely it's a question of the used version.
As far as I know the SSI-functionallity is included since version 2.5.
I use version 2.5b4 and the option is available exactly as Marcio =
describes it.
The best solution would be  to update your Xitami.
Otherwise you have to add to the filter-section of your defaults.cfg =
file:

   [Filter]
       shtml=3Dperlssi               #   Parse files with .shtml =
extension and pass it to perlssi which is a "FakeSSI"

and further the doku says:

#   The exec cmd=3D tag is only recognised if you set the environment =
variable
#   "SSI_INSECURE=3Dyes", in your autoexec.bat or system environment =
(for NT).



Best regards

Torsten

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Dec  6 15:28:10 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)
Date: Thu, 6 Dec 2001 10:28:10 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI
In-Reply-To: <B121AEA4C026D51180670000E899F02722F712@MAILSERVER>
Message-ID: <000a01c17e6a$9cc93630$0100a8c0@celeron2k>

	As far as I know Xitami has LRWP, not FastCGI. LRWP is not FastCGI, but it
is very similar. "The protocol between Xitami and the LRWP Peer is much
simpler than the FastCGI protocol, and therefore less prone to
implementation differences or errors. However, given the right circumstances
it is possible to run the same program as both a LRWP Peer and a FastCGI
Peer with only minor differences in the startup code. "


	So, you'd have to write your own C adapter to be a LRWP/FastCGI server &
link to the PHP/Perl interpreter.

	What I've seen in PHP (and probably Perl) under Win32 is that they support
the Microsoft way of doing things (ISAPI or something like that), which I
don't think Xitami supports ? Anyway, under PWS (Personal Web Server) and
IIS you can probably enable them in this faster mode (ISAPI).


	Again, maybe by now Xitami supports ISAPI, but I don't think so. I think
they don't because they want to be OS-portable, and ISAPI would be
Windows-specific. I could be wrong.

	Zope (www.zope.org) has a regular, thin CGI which then talks to Zope on a
specific port. So, if you configure Zope behind Apache, you use this
small&fast CGI which gets loaded/unloaded for every request, but it is
fast/small. It then opens a connection to Zope on a given socket, and they
exchange data, and the little CGI passes the bytes back to Apache. This is
another option, but you'd have to write the little CGI yourself and leave
the PHP or Perl interpreter running, listening for requests on a port (like
a Java servlet engine, etc). The advantage of this compared to an apache MOD
is that it is portable across web servers. You can run Zope behind any web
server just by porting this tiny CGI to the new platform. LRWP, on the other
ahnd, is Xitami-specific. MODs are Apache-specific. ISAPI is
Windows-specific. The Zope solution is very portable with a small
performance penalty (lightweight CGI + sockets). There's no ideal solution
:-)

	But Zope is designed to be a server & listen on a port, while the PHP/Perl
interpreters aren't. That's why they need more work, like a C code that
links to teh interpreter & does the glue work. It would be nice if Xitami
supported ISAPI.

	Sorry I don't have good news. Hope this helps a bit. Note that I may be
wrong in some points, it's been a while since I looked into this.

marcio

Hi!
Surely it's a question of the used version.
As far as I know the SSI-functionallity is included since version 2.5.
I use version 2.5b4 and the option is available exactly as Marcio =
describes it.
The best solution would be  to update your Xitami.
Otherwise you have to add to the filter-section of your defaults.cfg =
file:
=20
   [Filter]
       shtml=3Dperlssi               #   Parse files with .shtml =
extension and pass it to perlssi which is a "FakeSSI"

and further the doku says:

#   The exec cmd=3D tag is only recognised if you set the environment =
variable
#   "SSI_INSECURE=3Dyes", in your autoexec.bat or system environment =
(for NT).



Best regards
=20
Torsten

filter-section of your defaults.cfg file:</FONT></DIV>
<DIV><FONT face=3DArial size=3D2></FONT>&nbsp;</DIV>
<DIV><FONT face=3DArial size=3D2>&nbsp;&nbsp;=20
[Filter]<BR>&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;=20
shtml=3Dperlssi&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbs=
p;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;=20
#&nbsp;&nbsp; Parse files with .shtml extension and pass it to perlssi =
which is=20
a "FakeSSI"</FONT></DIV>
<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>
<DIV><FONT face=3DArial size=3D2>and further the doku says:</FONT></DIV>
<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>
<DIV><FONT face=3DArial size=3D2>#&nbsp;&nbsp; The exec cmd=3D tag is =
only recognised=20
if you set the environment variable<BR>#&nbsp;&nbsp; =
"SSI_INSECURE=3Dyes", in your=20
autoexec.bat or system environment (for NT).<BR></FONT></DIV>
<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>
<DIV>&nbsp;</DIV>
<DIV><FONT face=3DArial size=3D2>Best regards</FONT></DIV>
<DIV><FONT face=3DArial size=3D2></FONT>&nbsp;</DIV>
<DIV><FONT face=3DArial size=3D2>Torsten</FONT></DIV>

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Dec  6 16:09:29 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Peter)
Date: Thu, 6 Dec 2001 11:09:29 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI
References: <000a01c17e6a$9cc93630$0100a8c0@celeron2k>
Message-ID: <001701c17e70$6a330510$205dddd8@LACKY>

I've spent the morning trying to get php running as ISAPI without any luck.
It sure looks like it should work the set-up is very similar to another
server I use. I don't seem to be getting any errors Xitami is servering the
test page but it is not processing the script.

The FAQ says:
  1.. First off, make sure Xitami is installed and running.
  2.. Next, download and install the PHP binary distribution into some
directory. We'll assume it's c:\php.
  3.. Add '.php=c:\php\php.exe' to the Filter section of the Xitami
confguration.
  4.. Rename the PHP initialisation file, 'php3.ini-dist' to 'php3.ini' and
copy it into the Windows directory. Don't bother trying to set the PHPRC
environment variable, because this does not seem to work.
  5.. Edit the ini file and change the 'extension_dir' setting to c:\php.
  6.. Now test PHP by hand with a small test page, by running it in a
command window, in the Xitami directory:
c:\php\php webpages\test.php


----- Original Message -----
From: "Marcio Marchini" <mqm@magma.ca>
To: <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
Sent: Thursday, December 06, 2001 10:28 AM
Subject: RE: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI


>
> As far as I know Xitami has LRWP, not FastCGI. LRWP is not FastCGI, but it
> is very similar. "The protocol between Xitami and the LRWP Peer is much
> simpler than the FastCGI protocol, and therefore less prone to
> implementation differences or errors. However, given the right
circumstances
> it is possible to run the same program as both a LRWP Peer and a FastCGI
> Peer with only minor differences in the startup code. "
>
>
> So, you'd have to write your own C adapter to be a LRWP/FastCGI server &
> link to the PHP/Perl interpreter.
>
> What I've seen in PHP (and probably Perl) under Win32 is that they support
> the Microsoft way of doing things (ISAPI or something like that), which I
> don't think Xitami supports ? Anyway, under PWS (Personal Web Server) and
> IIS you can probably enable them in this faster mode (ISAPI).
>
>
> Again, maybe by now Xitami supports ISAPI, but I don't think so. I think
> they don't because they want to be OS-portable, and ISAPI would be
> Windows-specific. I could be wrong.
>
> Zope (www.zope.org) has a regular, thin CGI which then talks to Zope on a
> specific port. So, if you configure Zope behind Apache, you use this
> small&fast CGI which gets loaded/unloaded for every request, but it is
> fast/small. It then opens a connection to Zope on a given socket, and they
> exchange data, and the little CGI passes the bytes back to Apache. This is
> another option, but you'd have to write the little CGI yourself and leave
> the PHP or Perl interpreter running, listening for requests on a port
(like
> a Java servlet engine, etc). The advantage of this compared to an apache
MOD
> is that it is portable across web servers. You can run Zope behind any web
> server just by porting this tiny CGI to the new platform. LRWP, on the
other
> ahnd, is Xitami-specific. MODs are Apache-specific. ISAPI is
> Windows-specific. The Zope solution is very portable with a small
> performance penalty (lightweight CGI + sockets). There's no ideal solution
> :-)
>
> But Zope is designed to be a server & listen on a port, while the PHP/Perl
> interpreters aren't. That's why they need more work, like a C code that
> links to teh interpreter & does the glue work. It would be nice if Xitami
> supported ISAPI.
>
> Sorry I don't have good news. Hope this helps a bit. Note that I may be
> wrong in some points, it's been a while since I looked into this.
>
> marcio
>
>

> > From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org

> > has been raised many time, there has
> > been no post telling 'yes i've done it and here is the url'.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Dec  6 16:31:21 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)
Date: Thu, 6 Dec 2001 11:31:21 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI
In-Reply-To: <001701c17e70$6a330510$205dddd8@LACKY>
Message-ID: <000e01c17e73$7050b200$0100a8c0@celeron2k>

	If it is just serving the file instead of executing it, add this to your
defaults.cfg:

[Mime]
.php=application/x-httpd-php
.php3=application/x-httpd-php3



	I've had the same problem with regular CGI stuff.

marcio

If I enter some thing like "^062\b" when I submit it I end up with "^062\\b" (note the double slash).

Can some one tell me who is doing me this favor of escaping things for me, and how do I prevent it?


    <FORM method='post' action='pbsearchresult.php'>
      <INPUT type="hidden" name='cmd' value='search'> <INPUT type=
      "text" name='data' value='^062.* 8.*MHz'> <INPUT type="submit"
      name='do' value=
      'Search with (POSIX-style) regular expression'><BR>
    </FORM>

    echo "You are searching for <B>$data</B>:<BR>\n";

From: "Marcio Marchini" <mqm@magma.ca>

Sent: Thursday, December 06, 2001 11:31 AM
Subject: RE: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI

> defaults.cfg:
>
> [Mime]
> .php=application/x-httpd-php
> .php3=application/x-httpd-php3
>
>
>
> I've had the same problem with regular CGI stuff.
>
> marcio
>
> > -----Original Message-----
> > From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org
> > [mailto:xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org]On Behalf Of Peter
> > Sent: December 6, 2001 11:09 AM
> > To: xitami@lists.xitami.org
> > Subject: Re: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI
> >
> >
> > I've spent the morning trying to get php running as ISAPI without
> > any luck.
> > It sure looks like it should work the set-up is very similar to another
> > server I use. I don't seem to be getting any errors Xitami is
> > servering the
> > test page but it is not processing the script.
> >
> > The FAQ says:
> >   1.. First off, make sure Xitami is installed and running.
> >   2.. Next, download and install the PHP binary distribution into some
> > directory. We'll assume it's c:\php.
> >   3.. Add '.php=c:\php\php.exe' to the Filter section of the Xitami
> > confguration.
> >   4.. Rename the PHP initialisation file, 'php3.ini-dist' to
> > 'php3.ini' and
> > copy it into the Windows directory. Don't bother trying to set the PHPRC
> > environment variable, because this does not seem to work.
> >   5.. Edit the ini file and change the 'extension_dir' setting to
c:\php.
> >   6.. Now test PHP by hand with a small test page, by running it in a
> > command window, in the Xitami directory:
> > c:\php\php webpages\test.php
> >
> >
> > ----- Original Message -----
> > From: "Marcio Marchini" <mqm@magma.ca>
> > To: <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
> > Sent: Thursday, December 06, 2001 10:28 AM
> > Subject: RE: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI
> >
> >
> > >
> > > As far as I know Xitami has LRWP, not FastCGI. LRWP is not
> > FastCGI, but it
> > > is very similar. "The protocol between Xitami and the LRWP Peer is
much
> > > simpler than the FastCGI protocol, and therefore less prone to
> > > implementation differences or errors. However, given the right
> > circumstances
> > > it is possible to run the same program as both a LRWP Peer and a
FastCGI
> > > Peer with only minor differences in the startup code. "
> > >
> > >
> > > So, you'd have to write your own C adapter to be a LRWP/FastCGI server
&
> > > link to the PHP/Perl interpreter.
> > >
> > > What I've seen in PHP (and probably Perl) under Win32 is that
> > they support
> > > the Microsoft way of doing things (ISAPI or something like
> > that), which I
> > > don't think Xitami supports ? Anyway, under PWS (Personal Web
> > Server) and
> > > IIS you can probably enable them in this faster mode (ISAPI).
> > >
> > >
> > > Again, maybe by now Xitami supports ISAPI, but I don't think so. I
think
> > > they don't because they want to be OS-portable, and ISAPI would be
> > > Windows-specific. I could be wrong.
> > >
> > > Zope (www.zope.org) has a regular, thin CGI which then talks to
> > Zope on a
> > > specific port. So, if you configure Zope behind Apache, you use this
> > > small&fast CGI which gets loaded/unloaded for every request, but it is
> > > fast/small. It then opens a connection to Zope on a given
> > socket, and they
> > > exchange data, and the little CGI passes the bytes back to
> > Apache. This is
> > > another option, but you'd have to write the little CGI yourself
> > and leave
> > > the PHP or Perl interpreter running, listening for requests on a port
> > (like
> > > a Java servlet engine, etc). The advantage of this compared to an
apache
> > MOD
> > > is that it is portable across web servers. You can run Zope
> > behind any web
> > > server just by porting this tiny CGI to the new platform. LRWP, on the
> > other
> > > ahnd, is Xitami-specific. MODs are Apache-specific. ISAPI is
> > > Windows-specific. The Zope solution is very portable with a small
> > > performance penalty (lightweight CGI + sockets). There's no
> > ideal solution
> > > :-)
> > >
> > > But Zope is designed to be a server & listen on a port, while
> > the PHP/Perl
> > > interpreters aren't. That's why they need more work, like a C code
that
> > > links to teh interpreter & does the glue work. It would be nice
> > if Xitami
> > > supported ISAPI.
> > >
> > > Sorry I don't have good news. Hope this helps a bit. Note that I may
be
> > > wrong in some points, it's been a while since I looked into this.
> > >
> > > marcio
> > >
> > >
> > > > -----Original Message-----

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Dec  6 16:52:48 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)
Date: Thu, 6 Dec 2001 11:52:48 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI
In-Reply-To: <001701c17e70$6a330510$205dddd8@LACKY>
Message-ID: <001001c17e76$6f908ef0$0100a8c0@celeron2k>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_0011_01C17E4C.86BA86F0
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit



        BTW, there's a PHP download which automatically configures Xitami.
It has a wizard that does it all. It's the MSI download for PHP, not the zip
version. The problem with that is that it does not come with all the
extensions compiled in. You may not care, though.

        Also, the way you are doing seems to be regular CGI, not ISAPI. For
ISAPI you tell the web server which DLL to load. When you point to the EXE,
it's usually non-ISAPI, but regular CGI.  See
http://www.dynamic-webpages.de/php/install.iis.php

----- cut here ------

If you choose the CGI binary, do the following:
Edit the enclosed pws-php4cgi.reg file (look into the sapi dir) to reflect
the location of your php.exe. Forward slashes should be escaped, for
example:
[HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Services\w3svc\parameters\Scrip
t Map] ".php"="c:\\php\\php.exe"


If you choose the ISAPI module, do the following:
Edit the enclosed pws-php4isapi.reg file (look into the sapi dir) to reflect
the location of your php4isapi.dll. Forward slashes should be escaped, for
example:
[HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Services\w3svc\parameters\Scrip
t Map] ".php"="c:\\php\\sapi\\php4isapi.dll"

----- cut here ------

    Again, I am not sure Xitami supports ISAPI.

marcio

Here is what I get from the debug.log

2001/12/06 11:53:59: - URL handled by filter 'c:\php\php.exe'
2001/12/06 11:53:59: - request refers to a normal readable file
2001/12/06 11:53:59: Transfer file=C:\WINNT\TEMP\pipe0001.flt size=0 from=0



----- Original Message -----
From: "Marcio Marchini" <mqm@magma.ca>
To: <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
Sent: Thursday, December 06, 2001 11:31 AM
Subject: RE: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI


>
> If it is just serving the file instead of executing it, add this to your
> defaults.cfg:
>
> [Mime]
> .php=application/x-httpd-php
> .php3=application/x-httpd-php3
>
>
>
> I've had the same problem with regular CGI stuff.
>
> marcio
>
> > -----Original Message-----
> > From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org
> > [mailto:xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org]On Behalf Of Peter
> > Sent: December 6, 2001 11:09 AM
> > To: xitami@lists.xitami.org
> > Subject: Re: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI
> >
> >
> > I've spent the morning trying to get php running as ISAPI without
> > any luck.
> > It sure looks like it should work the set-up is very similar to another
> > server I use. I don't seem to be getting any errors Xitami is
> > servering the
> > test page but it is not processing the script.
> >
> > The FAQ says:
> >   1.. First off, make sure Xitami is installed and running.
> >   2.. Next, download and install the PHP binary distribution into some
> > directory. We'll assume it's c:\php.
> >   3.. Add '.php=c:\php\php.exe' to the Filter section of the Xitami
> > confguration.
> >   4.. Rename the PHP initialisation file, 'php3.ini-dist' to
> > 'php3.ini' and
> > copy it into the Windows directory. Don't bother trying to set the PHPRC
> > environment variable, because this does not seem to work.
> >   5.. Edit the ini file and change the 'extension_dir' setting to
c:\php.
> >   6.. Now test PHP by hand with a small test page, by running it in a
> > command window, in the Xitami directory:
> > c:\php\php webpages\test.php
> >
> >
> > ----- Original Message -----
> > From: "Marcio Marchini" <mqm@magma.ca>
> > To: <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
> > Sent: Thursday, December 06, 2001 10:28 AM
> > Subject: RE: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI
> >
> >
> > >
> > > As far as I know Xitami has LRWP, not FastCGI. LRWP is not
> > FastCGI, but it
> > > is very similar. "The protocol between Xitami and the LRWP Peer is
much
> > > simpler than the FastCGI protocol, and therefore less prone to
> > > implementation differences or errors. However, given the right
> > circumstances
> > > it is possible to run the same program as both a LRWP Peer and a
FastCGI
> > > Peer with only minor differences in the startup code. "
> > >
> > >
> > > So, you'd have to write your own C adapter to be a LRWP/FastCGI server
&
> > > link to the PHP/Perl interpreter.
> > >
> > > What I've seen in PHP (and probably Perl) under Win32 is that
> > they support
> > > the Microsoft way of doing things (ISAPI or something like
> > that), which I
> > > don't think Xitami supports ? Anyway, under PWS (Personal Web
> > Server) and
> > > IIS you can probably enable them in this faster mode (ISAPI).
> > >
> > >
> > > Again, maybe by now Xitami supports ISAPI, but I don't think so. I
think
> > > they don't because they want to be OS-portable, and ISAPI would be
> > > Windows-specific. I could be wrong.
> > >
> > > Zope (www.zope.org) has a regular, thin CGI which then talks to
> > Zope on a
> > > specific port. So, if you configure Zope behind Apache, you use this
> > > small&fast CGI which gets loaded/unloaded for every request, but it is
> > > fast/small. It then opens a connection to Zope on a given
> > socket, and they
> > > exchange data, and the little CGI passes the bytes back to
> > Apache. This is
> > > another option, but you'd have to write the little CGI yourself
> > and leave
> > > the PHP or Perl interpreter running, listening for requests on a port
> > (like
> > > a Java servlet engine, etc). The advantage of this compared to an
apache
> > MOD
> > > is that it is portable across web servers. You can run Zope
> > behind any web
> > > server just by porting this tiny CGI to the new platform. LRWP, on the
> > other
> > > ahnd, is Xitami-specific. MODs are Apache-specific. ISAPI is
> > > Windows-specific. The Zope solution is very portable with a small
> > > performance penalty (lightweight CGI + sockets). There's no
> > ideal solution
> > > :-)
> > >
> > > But Zope is designed to be a server & listen on a port, while
> > the PHP/Perl
> > > interpreters aren't. That's why they need more work, like a C code
that
> > > links to teh interpreter & does the glue work. It would be nice
> > if Xitami
> > > supported ISAPI.
> > >
> > > Sorry I don't have good news. Hope this helps a bit. Note that I may
be
> > > wrong in some points, it's been a while since I looked into this.
> > >
> > > marcio
> > >
> > >
> > > > -----Original Message-----
> > > > From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org
> > > > [mailto:xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org]On Behalf Of Vardhan Varma
> > > > Sent: December 5, 2001 11:04 PM
> > > > To: 'xitami@lists.xitami.org'
> > > > Subject: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI
> > > >
> > > >
> > > >
> > > >  Hi,
> > > >   I've searched the archive, and while the question of PHP and PERL
> > > > as non-CGI (fastcgi/WSX etc and not seperate process executed
> > everytime)
> > > > has been raised many time, there has
> > > > been no post telling 'yes i've done it and here is the url'.
> > > >
> > > > Does anybody has PHP/perl running as non-CGI in Xitami ?
> > > > If yes, are they willing to share the patch .
> > > >

I'm not using IIS but I see your point. I just checked my working server and
this is my mapping for php. I will give this a try with the Xitami

*.phtml *.php3 *.php = C:/php/sapi/php4isapi.dll


----- Original Message -----
From: "Marcio Marchini" <mqm@magma.ca>
To: <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
Sent: Thursday, December 06, 2001 11:52 AM
Subject: RE: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI


>
>
>         BTW, there's a PHP download which automatically configures Xitami.
> It has a wizard that does it all. It's the MSI download for PHP, not the
zip
> version. The problem with that is that it does not come with all the
> extensions compiled in. You may not care, though.
>
>         Also, the way you are doing seems to be regular CGI, not ISAPI.
For
> ISAPI you tell the web server which DLL to load. When you point to the
EXE,
> it's usually non-ISAPI, but regular CGI.  See
> http://www.dynamic-webpages.de/php/install.iis.php
>
> ----- cut here ------
>
> If you choose the CGI binary, do the following:
> Edit the enclosed pws-php4cgi.reg file (look into the sapi dir) to reflect
> the location of your php.exe. Forward slashes should be escaped, for
> example:
>
[HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Services\w3svc\parameters\Scrip
> t Map] ".php"="c:\\php\\php.exe"
>
>
> If you choose the ISAPI module, do the following:
> Edit the enclosed pws-php4isapi.reg file (look into the sapi dir) to
reflect
> the location of your php4isapi.dll. Forward slashes should be escaped, for
> example:
>
[HKEY_LOCAL_MACHINE\SYSTEM\CurrentControlSet\Services\w3svc\parameters\Scrip
> t Map] ".php"="c:\\php\\sapi\\php4isapi.dll"
>
> ----- cut here ------
>
>     Again, I am not sure Xitami supports ISAPI.
>
> marcio
>

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Dec  6 17:06:31 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)
Date: Thu, 6 Dec 2001 12:06:31 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI
In-Reply-To: <000f01c17e75$e7e40b80$205dddd8@LACKY>
Message-ID: <001801c17e78$5a1d00b0$0100a8c0@celeron2k>

	Did you remember to stop/start the server ? It may not be reading the
config file. It may be configured to re-read every 60 seconds, etc.

	But, as I said, this is not ISAPI, it's CGI. For that (CGI), either you use
the PHP MSI install to have it all done automatically, or by hand like this:

1) Add this to the end of c:\xitami\defaults.cfg

[Filter]
php=c:\php\php.exe

[Mime]
.php=application/x-httpd-php3


2) Restart the server

	(which assumes you already have PHP installed, under c:\php)

	I just saw that ISAPI for Xitami is still a beta - see
http://www.xitami.com/addons.htm


marcio

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Dec  6 18:22:42 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Owen Rudge)
Date: Thu, 6 Dec 2001 18:22:42 -0000
Subject: [Xitami] Regular Expression escaping?
References: <200112061149968.SM00191@BOB-PADDOCK>
Message-ID: <018d01c17e83$00c1c900$1d91fc3e@rudge>

> Can some one tell me who is doing me this favor of escaping things for me,
and how do I prevent it?

The PHP magic_quotes variables in php.ini do this. Search php.ini for
magic_quotes, and you'll find three items along with a bit of documentation.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Dec  6 18:36:33 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)

Subject: [Xitami] Regular Expression escaping?
In-Reply-To: <200112061149968.SM00191@BOB-PADDOCK>

	I use the stripslashes function in PHP to get the original value back:

function stripFormSlashes() {
    global $newQuestion;
    ...

    $newQuestion = stripslashes ($newQuestion);
    ...
}


	But that's a PHP issue, not a Xitami issue. Try www.php.net for that.

> >on a win 98 machine and now I need it on a Windows 2000 but i can't seem

	Personally I don't think it is possible to get a "HTTP port 80-Port is
already used by another server (WSAEADDRINUSE) " and not have anything show
up under netstat.


http://www.catalyst.com/support/help/visual/swrench/errors/wsaeaddrinuse.htm
l
WSAEADDRINUSE
Specified address is already in use
This error is usually generated when an application attempts to create a
listening socket and specifies an address that is in use, or if the socket
is already listening for connections. This error can also occur if the
LocalPort property is set to a non-zero value and the port is being used by
another application. Client applications should typically reset the value of
the LocalPort property to zero before attempting to connect to a remote
host.



http://support.exceloncorp.com/whitepapers/troubleshooting_connection_proble
ms.html
WSAEADDRINUSE:
the application attempts to bind a socket to an IP address/port that has
already been used for an existing socket, or a socket that wasn't closed
properly, or one that is still in the process of closing.



marcio

Hello,

I got Xitami 'cause I got tired of someone else running my server for me,
and telling me what I can and can't do.  I can, and have, spent all day
looking around the internet for pre-made CGI scritpts with idiot
step-by-step instructions on how to install it, and have the script do
almost what I want it to do.

But, I would really rather make my own scripts that do exactly what I want
them to do.  I don't even really know what I want them to do yet.  I am
inspired by discovered possibilty.

I am a programmer by trade, but I am still very new to any sort of internet
programming.  I mainly know old-school (GW BASIC, FORTRAN, COBOL) and  a
half-dozen very proprietary languages.  Currently my Xitami FTP/HTTP server
is running on Windows ME.

I was wondering if anyone could help me with:

A) What would be a good first scripting method to begin with on Xitami?
(PHP,  Perl, etc.)

B) Where are the good beginner tutorial sites, PDFs available for this type
of scripting?

Thanks in advance for any help.

Jay Aldrich


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Dec  6 21:44:36 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)
Date: Thu, 6 Dec 2001 16:44:36 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] CGI School
In-Reply-To: <01b301c17e97$cac11ee0$b61e2341@concentric.net>
Message-ID: <002c01c17e9f$33358590$0100a8c0@celeron2k>

> A) What would be a good first scripting method to begin with on Xitami?
> (PHP,  Perl, etc.)


	If you want to do web apps/CGI, I suggest PHP. It reads well, it's easy to
learn, OS- and webserver-portable, and has plenty of resources online.

	If you already know programming and like a "How do I... ?" kind of book, I
recommend "PHP Developer's Cookbook" to get started quickly.

	As far as online stuff there's www.php.net, and you can download a
Microsoft Help file from it, all hyperlinked, with the PHP documentation.

	You can probably search for goodies instead of writing them.
www.freshmeat.net, for example.

	For instance, for sharing digital pictures, you may want to use Gallery
(http://gallery.sourceforge.net/). For portal stuff, PHP Nuke
(http://www.phpnuke.org), and so on.

	You may need to install MySQL for some apps. Some apps may not support
windows, just UNIX.

marcio

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Dec  7 00:20:54 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul N Shortis)
Date: Fri, 7 Dec 2001 10:20:54 +1000
Subject: [Xitami] CGI School
Message-ID: <4A256B1B.0001F9DB.00@shb1ln11.transport.qld.gov.au>


I am a developer of some 20 years experience C, C++, SQL etc. & have both 'PHP
Developers Cookbook' and 'A Programmers Introduction tp PHP 4.0 by W.J. Gilmore
- printed by Apress. At first I thought that the second book was a little light
on, then bought 'PHP Developers Cookbook' only to learn then A Programmers
Introduction tp PHP 4.0 was far more useful. They both have their place, but A
Programmers Introduction tp PHP 4.0 is a far better start and doesn't rely so
much on referring you the php's CURL library as 'PHP Developers Cookbook'.

You should also look at www.hotscripts.com and
http://www.phpclasses.upperdesign.com for loads of pre-written scripts and
classes.

Paul


> A) What would be a good first scripting method to begin with on Xitami?
> (PHP,  Perl, etc.)


     If you want to do web apps/CGI, I suggest PHP. It reads well, it's easy to
learn, OS- and webserver-portable, and has plenty of resources online.

     If you already know programming and like a "How do I... ?" kind of book, I
recommend "PHP Developer's Cookbook" to get started quickly.

     As far as online stuff there's www.php.net, and you can download a
Microsoft Help file from it, all hyperlinked, with the PHP documentation.

     You can probably search for goodies instead of writing them.
www.freshmeat.net, for example.

     For instance, for sharing digital pictures, you may want to use Gallery
(http://gallery.sourceforge.net/). For portal stuff, PHP Nuke
(http://www.phpnuke.org), and so on.

     You may need to install MySQL for some apps. Some apps may not support
windows, just UNIX.

marcio

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Dec  7 00:30:46 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul N Shortis)
Date: Fri, 7 Dec 2001 10:30:46 +1000
Subject: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI
Message-ID: <4A256B1B.0002DEF2.00@shb1ln11.transport.qld.gov.au>


This happens when Xitami runs php.exe but php.exe can't locate the php4ts.dll,
either add the path to php.exe/php4ts.dll to your system environment or move
php4ts.dll to your system directory (e.g. c:\winnt\system32. This happens so
often that I think it should be somewhere in the Xitami documentation.

I haven't had time to investigate, however I suspect it may be because xitami
doesn't make the directory that php.exe is in the current working directory
before launching php.exe, apache doesn't have this problem so it isn't simply
just a 'php issue' just the combination of the way xitami and php work.

Paul

> >   1.. First off, make sure Xitami is installed and running.
> >   2.. Next, download and install the PHP binary distribution into some
> > directory. We'll assume it's c:\php.
> >   3.. Add '.php=c:\php\php.exe' to the Filter section of the Xitami
> > confguration.
> >   4.. Rename the PHP initialisation file, 'php3.ini-dist' to
> > 'php3.ini' and
> > copy it into the Windows directory. Don't bother trying to set the PHPRC
> > environment variable, because this does not seem to work.
> >   5.. Edit the ini file and change the 'extension_dir' setting to
c:\php.

> > command window, in the Xitami directory:

> > ----- Original Message -----
> > From: "Marcio Marchini" <mqm@magma.ca>
> > To: <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
> > Sent: Thursday, December 06, 2001 10:28 AM
> > Subject: RE: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI
> >
> >
> > >
> > > As far as I know Xitami has LRWP, not FastCGI. LRWP is not
> > FastCGI, but it
> > > is very similar. "The protocol between Xitami and the LRWP Peer is
much
> > > simpler than the FastCGI protocol, and therefore less prone to
> > > implementation differences or errors. However, given the right
> > circumstances
> > > it is possible to run the same program as both a LRWP Peer and a
FastCGI
> > > Peer with only minor differences in the startup code. "
> > >
> > >
> > > So, you'd have to write your own C adapter to be a LRWP/FastCGI server
&
> > > link to the PHP/Perl interpreter.
> > >
> > > What I've seen in PHP (and probably Perl) under Win32 is that
> > they support
> > > the Microsoft way of doing things (ISAPI or something like
> > that), which I
> > > don't think Xitami supports ? Anyway, under PWS (Personal Web
> > Server) and
> > > IIS you can probably enable them in this faster mode (ISAPI).
> > >
> > >
> > > Again, maybe by now Xitami supports ISAPI, but I don't think so. I
think
> > > they don't because they want to be OS-portable, and ISAPI would be
> > > Windows-specific. I could be wrong.
> > >
> > > Zope (www.zope.org) has a regular, thin CGI which then talks to
> > Zope on a
> > > specific port. So, if you configure Zope behind Apache, you use this
> > > small&fast CGI which gets loaded/unloaded for every request, but it is
> > > fast/small. It then opens a connection to Zope on a given
> > socket, and they
> > > exchange data, and the little CGI passes the bytes back to
> > Apache. This is
> > > another option, but you'd have to write the little CGI yourself
> > and leave
> > > the PHP or Perl interpreter running, listening for requests on a port
> > (like
> > > a Java servlet engine, etc). The advantage of this compared to an
apache
> > MOD
> > > is that it is portable across web servers. You can run Zope
> > behind any web
> > > server just by porting this tiny CGI to the new platform. LRWP, on the
> > other
> > > ahnd, is Xitami-specific. MODs are Apache-specific. ISAPI is
> > > Windows-specific. The Zope solution is very portable with a small
> > > performance penalty (lightweight CGI + sockets). There's no
> > ideal solution
> > > :-)
> > >
> > > But Zope is designed to be a server & listen on a port, while
> > the PHP/Perl
> > > interpreters aren't. That's why they need more work, like a C code
that
> > > links to teh interpreter & does the glue work. It would be nice
> > if Xitami
> > > supported ISAPI.
> > >
> > > Sorry I don't have good news. Hope this helps a bit. Note that I may
be
> > > wrong in some points, it's been a while since I looked into this.
> > >
> > > marcio
> > >
> > >

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Dec  7 01:06:32 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul N Shortis)
Date: Fri, 7 Dec 2001 11:06:32 +1000
Subject: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI
Message-ID: <4A256B1B.0006264C.00@shb1ln11.transport.qld.gov.au>


In the php.ini file the extension directory should be set to

c:\php\extensions

If you use the standard php install ('cos that's where the extensions are
installed, they won't be found anywhere else :-) )

Paul




"Peter" <peter@iwebsl.com> on 07/12/2001 02:09:29 AM

Please respond to xitami@lists.xitami.org

To:   xitami@lists.xitami.org
cc:    (bcc: Paul N Shortis/Roads/QMR/Au)
Subject:  Re: [Xitami] PHP/perl as non-CGI



I've spent the morning trying to get php running as ISAPI without any luck.
It sure looks like it should work the set-up is very similar to another
server I use. I don't seem to be getting any errors Xitami is servering the
test page but it is not processing the script.

The FAQ says:
  1.. First off, make sure Xitami is installed and running.
  2.. Next, download and install the PHP binary distribution into some
directory. We'll assume it's c:\php.
  3.. Add '.php=c:\php\php.exe' to the Filter section of the Xitami
confguration.
  4.. Rename the PHP initialisation file, 'php3.ini-dist' to 'php3.ini' and
copy it into the Windows directory. Don't bother trying to set the PHPRC
environment variable, because this does not seem to work.
  5.. Edit the ini file and change the 'extension_dir' setting to c:\php.
  6.. Now test PHP by hand with a small test page, by running it in a
command window, in the Xitami directory:
c:\php\php webpages\test.php

>
>I am a programmer by trade, but I am still very new to any sort of internet

>is running on Windows ME.
>

>
>A) What would be a good first scripting method to begin with on Xitami?
>(PHP,  Perl, etc.)

hello

if you're new to scripting, but you can program in basic, you should stay 
to basic !!!! (lots of exclamation points here)
look at ALL the 'help-me' messages about perl & PHP :-) if that is not a 
clue about selecting a language...
i tried perl years ago and it was not a success...
keep your scripting talents if you have some to <script 
language=javascript> in html.
a script is converted at execute time and then executed, an executable is 
already compiled and ready for execution.

you can use visual basic (if you are used to it), but it's like an overkill 
(whenever a visual basic exe is loaded to be executed, other things not 
needed are also loaded).

Xitami will even accept old quickbasic code! (xitami will try to execute 
everyting is executable, even batch files).

i only use powerbasic for 3 (three) days, and i love it!
It has all the needed things to perform string operations (lots of command 
that lack in visual basic and other basic languages like seach-and-replace, 
crop, regular expressions, and so on). And because it's a console program 
(like for instance tracert and ping) it has the power of a 32 application, 
but not the overhead of loading graphics and forms.

Power basic is also network-aware. For instance, you can send mail in let's 
say 5 lines of code (it's not as simple and easy as the 'sendmail' program 
in *nix but it does it job well).

You only need some code to get all the form data into the right variables 
and you print it to the client using PRINT#
I can send you sample code that i use on my site.

Sone nice feature of powerbasic is it's error handling. basically when an 
error occurs, it will continue with the next statement (that's the best 
thing to do, it seems to me) so you don't get an HTTP 500 (internet server 
error)
if needed, you can trap errors visual basic-like.

There are probably other basic flavors floating around that can do the same 
job.

Marc

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Dec  7 11:23:09 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Fri, 07 Dec 2001 12:23:09 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Emulating Apache directories
Message-ID: <3C10A69D.20200@freesbee.fr>

One useful thing that you can do in Apache is display a README file at 
the bottom of a directory listing. I tried to do the same thing using 
GSL in xitami and it works most of the time (code below). Where it 
doesn't work is where the directory is an alias to somewhere.

But there is one problemette. Xitami doesn't seem to give me the real 
directory path only the url path so I'm having to hack that to try and 
create the fully qualified filename I want to include in the listing. I 
had a look in the source and it looks like the function in smthttpl.c 
called http_list_directory is the what creates the xml tree for the 
script and it unfortunately doesn't seem to put such a variable in the tree.

Francis
-------

.readme = 'c:/xitami/webpages'+urlbase+'README'
.if exists (readme)
Readme file: 'README'
  <pre>
.  literal from readme
  </pre><hr>
.elsif exists (readme+'.txt')
Readme file: 'README.txt'
  <pre>
.  literal from readme+'.txt'
  </pre><hr>
.endif


Francis

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Dec  7 22:34:09 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 08 Dec 2001 11:34:09 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] dir access
In-Reply-To: Message from "Vastdeath" <vastdeath@yahoo.com>
 of "Fri, 07 Dec 2001 16:31:46 CDT." <001d01c17f66$92873210$6401a8c0@vastdeath>
Message-ID: <200112072234.LAA08193@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <001d01c17f66$92873210$6401a8c0@vastdeath>, "Vastdeath" writes:
>hey, I setup an alias to another directory of my hd

Add:

[alias]
   aliasname=directorypath

to the approriate virtual host configuration file (or defaults.cfg if
you are not using virtual hosts), and restart Xitami.  (You can also do
this through the web based admin.)

>and I wanted to know if I can deny get access from it, but allow 
>list access? this is with the http server

No.

You can do the reverse (allow GETs but refuse to provide a listing), but
not allow a listing and refuse to allow GETs.

If you just want people to be able to see what is there and not download
it I suggest you:
(a) don't use an alias
(b) create a HTML page (or a CGI to output one) that contains (outputs) 
    a list of files that are in that directory with whatever details
    you want.

The point of providing access to a directory is to allow people to
retrieve (GET) things from it; so it sounds to me like you don't want to
allow people access to the directory after all.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Dec  8 07:11:28 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (xitami@lists.xitami.org)
Date: Sat, 8 Dec 2001 01:11:28 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] CGI School
References: <01b301c17e97$cac11ee0$b61e2341@concentric.net> <008001c17ec2$a6e97f00$05fea8c0@jjb> <20011207164903.F419.SCOTT@therubberroom.org>
Message-ID: <000e01c17fb7$9044df60$05fea8c0@jjb>

Scott,
    As has been mentioned here, and I agree completely, each person will
have their favorite tools.....that said, I'd reply to your comment by saying
"you always get what you pay for"  :)

   PB comes with tools that parse form data very easily.  You basically use
a string buffer to put the contents in, then strip off the variable values.
To create the resulting page, you use a line similar to:

WriteCGI "<b>The result of your query " & Request$ & " is: " & ResultValue$
& </b>"

The real power happens between the post/get data and the WriteCGI sections.
Execution speed, even opening a sequential file, reading through it for a
specific value, closing and processing it is amazing, even on low end
hardware.  I'd be more than happy to email you some samples I've wipped
together.  There is also a ton of very impressive source code on the PB user
forums on PowerBasic's web site.

It all comes down to what you're comfortable with.  I think Bob Zale has
created an awesome product (ever since Borland TurboBasic), the support is
exceptional, and even though its not free, I find I can do things with PB
faster and easier than any other tool *most of the time* and to me, that's
worth paying for.   Your mileage may vary.  :)

--Joe

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Dec  8 07:28:15 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marc Doigny)
Date: Sat, 08 Dec 2001 08:28:15 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] CGI School
In-Reply-To: <20011207164903.F419.SCOTT@therubberroom.org>
References: <008001c17ec2$a6e97f00$05fea8c0@jjb>
 <01b301c17e97$cac11ee0$b61e2341@concentric.net>
 <008001c17ec2$a6e97f00$05fea8c0@jjb>
Message-ID: <5.0.2.1.2.20011208080747.01b1e5e0@190.190.190.1>

Hello !

It's not cheap, for a rather simple program, but if it's the right one, the 
money is well spend.
You don't need the DLL-version, only the console one, since you can 
#INCLUDE all the needed recurrent functions in your source (this will also 
speed execution, since there is no loading and linking of DLL's at run time).
If you have any programming experience in basic, writing complete programs 
in PB is easily done. It's a well structured language. It's that simple you 
don't need any tutorial. There is a windows help file included in the 
package for the case you're a newbee in basic.

Xitami will send your program the query string and even parse the form 
fields (if you use a <form method=POST ...> in your html source) by setting 
the environ. It's that simple i could't believe it at first!
And writing output to the browser is even more simple: you simply PRINT it 
to the provided temp-file!
I can mail you a small source code that sends the complete environment 
back, ideal for checking what Xitami actually sends to your program, 
depending on how you call the program.

There are all sorts of available basic routines for parsing data, but don't 
be fooled, you won't need them.

Marc

Content-Type: text/plain; charset="us-ascii"; format=flowed

At 08:11 8/12/01, you wrote:
>Scott,

[...]

>    PB comes with tools that parse form data very easily.  You basically use
>a string buffer to put the contents in, then strip off the variable values.
>To create the resulting page, you use a line similar to:

You normally don't need them.
Already done by Xitami.
Try it (source included, executable on my server).


>WriteCGI "<b>The result of your query " & Request$ & " is: " & ResultValue$
>& </b>"

Better still: simply open the output file and print to it.

That's all you actually need: NO SINGLE LINE MORE:

FUNCTION PBMAIN()                               ' main module is always 
named pbmain
     i = 1                                       ' execution begins here
                                                 ' Xitami creates a single 
temp name for
     OPEN ENVIRON$("CGI_STDOUT") FOR OUTPUT AS #3
                                                 ' the output file. You 
open it and
     PRINT #3, "<html><body><pre>"               ' write your html to it.
     a$ = ENVIRON$(i)                            ' This is a demo program. 
We iterate
     WHILE a$ <> ""                              ' over the complete 
environment and
         PRINT #3, a$; "<br>"                    ' print it out. Whenever 
ENVIRON$(i)
         i = i + 1                               ' gives you an empty 
string, we're done.
         a$ = ENVIRON$(i)                        ' You'll see all the named 
<input...>
     WEND                                        ' fields parsed in their 
respective name
     PRINT #3, "<hr>"
     OPEN ENVIRON$("CGI_STDIN") FOR INPUT AS #1  ' Xitami also gives you 
the complete
     WHILE NOT EOF(1)                            ' query string in a temp 
file. Here we
         LINE INPUT #1, a$                       ' simply open that file 
and output it
         PRINT #3, a$; "<br>"                    ' to the output file.
     WEND                                        ' Here we terminate the 
html output
     PRINT #3, "</body></html>"                  ' and end the program.
END FUNCTION                                    ' In this example, there is 
no error
                                                 ' trapping needed, the 
best thing to do
when an error occurs is to try to continue. The only error that can occur 
is a disk full.

Use a$ = REMAIN$(ENVIRON$(i), "=") to get only the value, not the complete 
equate.

ENVIRON$ can be used with named strings (when you know what you are looking 
for, that is when using form data or opening files provided by Xitami) or 
with an index (when you don't know what you are looking for).

This source can be optimised (using integer variables instead of floating 
point defaults and so on).

You can try this program out at <http://web.verfaillie.com/cgi-bin/env.exe>
Add query strings like you want 
<http://web.verfaillie.com/cgi-bin/env.exe?123ABC>

Or use a complete <form... > to call it. There is a sample one included 
with this mail.

Add the MIME type entry in your defaults.cfg

[Mime]
.pl=application/x-httpd-perl


I assume you already have this part:

[Filter]
pl=c:\perl\bin\perl.exe


marcio

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 10 06:24:24 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Dec 2001 19:24:24 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Emulating Apache directories
In-Reply-To: Message from Francis Turner <francis.turner@freesbee.fr>
 of "Fri, 07 Dec 2001 12:23:09 BST." <3C10A69D.20200@freesbee.fr>
Message-ID: <200112100624.TAA31826@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3C10A69D.20200@freesbee.fr>, Francis Turner writes:
>One useful thing that you can do in Apache is display a README file at 
>the bottom of a directory listing. I tried to do the same thing using 
>GSL in xitami and it works most of the time (code below). Where it 
>doesn't work is where the directory is an alias to somewhere.  [Because
>have to guess what the directory path on disk was]

Well spotted.  This is a bug (as far as I'm concerned), and I've added
it to our bug list.

You are right that smthttpl.c:http_list_directory() is what is creating
the directory (as an XML tree).  One of the things that it should also
add to the XML is the path to the actual directory on disk, since it
obviously needs to know this while it is preparing the list of files,
and it would be useful to the GSL script outputting the directory.  The
directory path is, I think, in p_http-> file_name, so adding an
attribute with that value into the top level of the XML would be useful,
called perhaps "path_on_disk".

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 10 06:41:34 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)

In message <002501c17d70$b80614e0$0ddcf4d0@dds.davidge.com>, "Erik A." writes:
>I don't see an
>"80...listen"  but i do see an 81.

Xitami tries to use port 81 for LRWP; but it's never actually had that
port reserved.  Perhaps somthing else is using port 81?  If so you might
want to try running Xitami with LRWP disabled, by adding:

[lrwp]
  enabled=0

to your defaults.cfg.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 10 06:52:00 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Dec 2001 19:52:00 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] How to limit number of simultaneous requests per IP?
In-Reply-To: Message from Sergey <oziris@russianteam.org>
 of "Sun, 02 Dec 2001 12:24:42 -0800." <3C0A8E0A.C220BC82@russianteam.org>
Message-ID: <200112100652.TAA32516@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3C0A8E0A.C220BC82@russianteam.org>, Sergey writes:
>Is there any way to limit number of simultaneous request per IP, or may
>be you know another way to disable webaccelerators?

There's not, currently, a way to limit the number of requests by IP
address.

One thing you might want to consider (in the 2.5 beta) is using the
bandwidth shaping feature, to limit the amount of traffic that is sent
out to particular locations -- so that they don't get any benefit from
making more than one request in parallel.  See pipedef.xml, and the
related documentation.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 10 06:55:42 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Dec 2001 19:55:42 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] IIS Coexistence
In-Reply-To: Message from test@emcom.co.uk
 of "Thu, 29 Nov 2001 22:18:50 -0000." <000801c17923$d5ffc550$01597ec2@tay>
Message-ID: <200112100655.TAA32712@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <000801c17923$d5ffc550$01597ec2@tay>, test@emcom.co.uk writes:
>I run Windows 2000 Professional and have IIIS installed. Can I run =
>xitami and IIS together?

Yes.  Either on different IP addresses (tell each one to use only a
specific IP address), or on different ports.  

>If I can, how can I direct my browser to correct site/virtual site?

If you use different IP addresses, use your hosts file, or the DNS, to
map from the names to the IP addresses for each server.  If you use
different ports, include the port number in the URL.

You can run Xitami on a different port using the "portbase" command line
option: -b BASE (which shifts _all_ port numbers up by that BASE
amount).

You can run Xitami on only one specific IP address by adding:

[server]  
  ipaddress=aaa.bbb.ccc.ddd

in your defaults.cfg and restarting Xitami.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 10 06:57:32 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Dec 2001 19:57:32 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Issues/questions with 2.5b5
In-Reply-To: Message from Scott Tyson <scott@therubberroom.org>
 of "Thu, 29 Nov 2001 08:50:51 -0800." <20011129084009.5C39.SCOTT@therubberroom.org>
Message-ID: <200112100657.TAA32730@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <20011129084009.5C39.SCOTT@therubberroom.org>, Scott Tyson writes:
>"Cannot spawn child process".  So my questions are:
>1. Can Xitami support PHP using aliases.

Not really, no.  In theory it should work, but in practice, it doesn't
at present.

>2. Can Xitami support PHP using DNS based vitual hosting (I need to host 3 doma
>ins on one IP address)

Yes, virtual hosts are fine with PHP -- in fact this is the recommended
work around for problems with PHP and aliases.

>3. Recomendations on how to run Xitami so it is not running as the system 
>account.  Just create a basic user like IIS does and give that user access 
>to only my WWW directories?

Yup, that's the easiest solution.  You can tell the Xitami service which
user to run as, and if you set up a uesr _just_ for Xitami (like IIS
does for itself) then you can restrict what it can do quite easily.

Ewen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 10 07:03:02 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Dec 2001 20:03:02 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Security
In-Reply-To: Message from "Johnson, Nathan J" <nathan.j.johnson@lmco.com>
 of "Tue, 27 Nov 2001 13:10:21 CDT." <9EFD49E2FB59D411AABA0008C7E675C005FB6BA0@emss04m10.ems.lmco.com>
Message-ID: <200112100703.UAA00522@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <9EFD49E2FB59D411AABA0008C7E675C005FB6BA0@emss04m10.ems.lmco.com>, "J
ohnson, Nathan J" writes:
>I was wondering if someone could post examples of their defaults.cfg etc.
>that have been optimized for maximum security.  Any other tips on enhancing
>security or other places to find information would be greatly appreciated.

It's hard to be specific about what to do without knowing which
operating system you are using.  The basic rules are: turn off
everything you don't need, try to run as a user that has the smallest
number of privileges necessary to do everything you need to, and make
sure that all the files are readable only by the user that needs access
to them.

There are other things to do if you're using scripting langauges (perl,
PHP, etc), but at that point it starts getting moderately specific to
your installation.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com
