In-Reply-To: Message from Jesse Foster <holyrunner@yahoo.com>
 of "Wed, 21 Nov 2001 20:30:23 -0800." <20011122043023.40086.qmail@web12508.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <200112100716.UAA00955@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <20011122043023.40086.qmail@web12508.mail.yahoo.com>, Jesse Foster writes:
>I found this line in the crash log.
>21/Nov/2001:18:11:38 -0500 Xitami v2.5b4
>Abort at smtsock:Send-Timeout-Event-To-Self: Getting-Event, No-Activity-Event)
>
>Anyone know what this means in English terms?

This is Xitami's (somewhat cryptic) debugging information.  It means
that while running smtsock (the module in Xitami that sends and receives
things over the network), in the "state" Send-Timeout-Event-To-Self, it
ran into problems with one of the events it mentions.  

Basically this shouldn't happen :-)

Unfortunately this sort of thing seems to happen occassionally, "at
random" which suggests that Xitami is occassionally being confused by
something, and crashing.

If we can track down any pattern of thing that reliably happens before a
problem like this, so that we can reproduce the problem, then it'll be
easier to fix.  Until then the best we can do is try to fix likely
causes of the problem.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Date: Mon, 10 Dec 2001 20:21:00 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Problems setting up xitami behind Roadrunner ISP
In-Reply-To: Message from "Control-Freak" <control-freak@cfl.rr.com>
 of "Wed, 21 Nov 2001 13:11:18 CDT." <008d01c172b7$eb955aa0$b61e2341@concentric.net>
Message-ID: <200112100721.UAA01141@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <008d01c172b7$eb955aa0$b61e2341@concentric.net>, "Control-Freak" writes:
>since Roadrunner blocks incoming port 80, I had to adust the portbase to
>55000 to use port 55080 with allows HTTP to work.  The problem is that I
>cannot get FTP to work at port 55021.
>So, I tried adjusting the FTP port varible to -54979 to get FTP port 21
>again.  But this does allow FTP to work either.  I also tried adjusting the
>data-port variable to -54800 to get the data port back down to 200.  

BTW, this data-port should probably be adjusted to be "20", ie, -54980.
(There was a typo in some versions of the configuration file that
wrongly listed the data port as 200.)

You should watch the Xitami start up messages and make sure that it is
starting things on the ports that you expect them to be started on.

Beyond that, FTP with the server behind a firewall (eg, your roadrunner
config) can be pretty tricky to get going, especially passive FTP when
the server is behind a firewall.  (Active FTP tends to work better when
the server is behind a firewall, and passive FTP tends to work better
when the client is behind a firewall -- if _both_ are behind firewalls,
you can end up with no FTP working at all, even if both firewalls are
trying to let FTP through :-( )

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 10 07:39:36 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Dec 2001 20:39:36 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Dynamic Ips
In-Reply-To: Message from Jesse Foster <holyrunner@yahoo.com>
 of "Sun, 11 Nov 2001 22:04:00 -0800." <20011112060400.63871.qmail@web12502.mail.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <200112100739.UAA02383@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <20011112060400.63871.qmail@web12502.mail.yahoo.com>, Jesse Foster writes:
>Does anyone know if it is possible to input a dynamic
>ip like <anything>.dyndns.org for an IP webmask which
>would allow access to the server?  

It's not.  It's a good idea, but it's not implemented that way at
present.  The way the webmasks work at present is that it converts the
IP address being considered into a dotted-quad (aaa.bbb.ccc.ddd) and
then compares it section by section.  This is to handle the wildcards.

SunOS 4?  (As opposed to Solaris 2.x, 7, 8, or 9)

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 10 08:00:40 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Dec 2001 21:00:40 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Webmask?? How do I block a list of IP addresses?
In-Reply-To: Message from "Alvaro E. Siman" <alsiman@cofs.net>
 of "Sun, 04 Nov 2001 20:17:28 CDT." <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCKEPHCDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
Message-ID: <200112100800.VAA03918@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCKEPHCDAA.alsiman@cofs.net>, "Alvaro E. Siman" wr
ites:
>My config looks like this:
>webmask=@blockiplist.txt

Yup.  Beware that there are _two_ webmask settings in the configuration
file (used for different things); make sure you're setting the right
one.  (Based on the section that the setting is in.)

>Now, what goes in that text file???  How do I type in the addresses??
>Should I put in the [webmask] at the top??

No [webmask] at the top.  Just list the IP addresses (with wildcards),
one per line.   Put a ! at the start to negate it.  Make sure you have
something to allow all the addresses you want allowed; the default is to
deny everything once you have a webmask list.  (If there's no webmask
list it allows everything.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Have you changed the webroot in defaults.cfg?  If so, there's a bug in
some versions of Xitami (including, I think, the released versions) that
means that this overrides _every_ webroot.  (It's fixed in the
development version in CVS.)

The Xitami server debugging is useful in tracking this down; to turn it
on set:

[server]   
  debug=1

then try again, then look at the debug logs to see what Xitami is basing
its returned things on.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 10 08:14:46 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Dec 2001 21:14:46 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] gslgen & xitami & errors
In-Reply-To: Message from Francis Turner <francis.turner@freesbee.fr>
 of "Thu, 25 Oct 2001 16:44:18 +0200." <3BD82542.2090505@freesbee.fr>
Message-ID: <200112100814.VAA05015@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3BD82542.2090505@freesbee.fr>, Francis Turner writes:
>But there are times when I'd like to abort the file and return an error. 
>Is it possible to return HTTP error codes? And if so is it also possible 
>to redirect people using a 302 return?

In theory this should work, _providing_ the HTTP headers come at the
very beginning.  The output of GSL is handled basically the same way as
a CGI's output in Xitami, and that means that some reparsing of headers
is done, so you should be able to output them _at_the_beginning_ and
have it work. 

Of course this means that you've got to figure out early on in your GSL
script (before outputting anything) if you want to give up and return an
error/redirect.

The solution you found (of using a meta-refresh) will work, but it's not
quite as tidy as a proper redirect for some things.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 10 08:20:23 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Dec 2001 21:20:23 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Rename log files: permission denied?
In-Reply-To: Message from Melle Koning <m.koning10@chello.nl>
 of "Tue, 23 Oct 2001 21:00:29 +0200." <1311492402.20011023210029@chello.nl>
Message-ID: <200112100820.VAA05246@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <1311492402.20011023210029@chello.nl>, Melle Koning writes:
>For the last seven days I see the following errors in the
>xitami-xidos32-console:
>Could not rename '.\logs\access.log to' '.\logs\ac011023.log'
>Permission denied
>[....]
>Is it possible that the logs are locked by MS Windows when there's a
>visitor on the site?

Not, really, no.  The logging module keeps the log files open when it is
running, but it is supposed to close them prior to trying to rename them.

So basically there's a few things that could be going on:
1.  The files are open for some reason, and so the log rotation fails
    (this would be a bug)

2.  The destination files exist for some reason (in which case Xitami
    is supposed to try some alternative names)

3.  The new files cannot be written for some reason (unlikely)

4.  The path names used internally for renaming the files are wrong
    (I've seen this happen in some older versions of Xitami.)

Running Xitami in server debug mode overnight:

[server]
  debug=1

in defaults.cfg may give you a little bit more information about what is
happening.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 10 08:28:48 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Dec 2001 21:28:48 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Question - 502 error message
In-Reply-To: Message from Richard.C.1@bwc.state.oh.us
 of "Thu, 18 Oct 2001 15:22:09 EDT." <6FDE0867413DD21182BF00A0C97251920755900A@MSWG4.bwc.state.oh.us>
Message-ID: <200112100828.VAA05988@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <6FDE0867413DD21182BF00A0C97251920755900A@MSWG4.bwc.state.oh.us>, Ric
hard.C.1@bwc.state.oh.us writes:
>When I run any test program, all is well. When I run a cgi program (that
>runs fine on my ISP with apache/unix), the browser "loading" bar at the
>bottom of the screen moves slowly then I get a 502 message saying that "The
>server is currently overloaded - please try again later". 

What this means is "it took too long".  Typically when you're testing 
that's not because the server is overloaded but because something your
CGI is trying to do is taking far too long.  Common things are looking
up names in the DNS, accessing a database, etc.  Basically in these
situations you have to try to figure out which bit it is that is taking
so long.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 10 08:32:26 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Dec 2001 21:32:26 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] FTP - LIST (ls) not returning wildcarded sub-dirs
In-Reply-To: Message from "Jeff Hamblin" <jphamblin@home.net>
 of "Mon, 15 Oct 2001 16:20:02 PDT." <006201c155d0$01190520$0300a8c0@aplusnet.com>
Message-ID: <200112100832.VAA06349@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <006201c155d0$01190520$0300a8c0@aplusnet.com>, "Jeff Hamblin" writes:
>The DT is sending a list request as follows:
>ftp> ls \dtf-tests\*\*Job.type
>200 Command okay
>150 Preparing to transfer ASCII file
>226 Closing data connection

That's because you probably don't have a file called "\dtf-tests\*\*Job.type".

Xitami can't expand wildcards in the same fancy way that unix FTP
servers do (generally by calling an external ls program to do it).

The FTP server in Xitami is intended to be a simple one to complement
the HTTP server.  If you need more advanced functions, then disable the
built in FTP server and use another one.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

> list already).

[Wsx]
  admin=""

works for me in defaults.cfg. That's 2.4d7 though. Asking for /admin
gives "501: not implemented" then.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 10 08:43:41 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 10 Dec 2001 21:43:41 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] block /admin
In-Reply-To: Message from Bernd Luevelsmeyer <bdluevel@heitec.net>
 of "Mon, 10 Dec 2001 09:32:48 BST." <20011210083248.DE44CB8101@christel.heitec.net>
Message-ID: <200112100843.VAA07303@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <20011210083248.DE44CB8101@christel.heitec.net>, Bernd Luevelsmeyer writes:
>Ewen McNeill wrote:
>> In message <018c01c16715$49549a60$0a00a8c0@enigmacomputers.com>, "Soulkoff" writes:
>> >Is there any way to get /admin to give a 404 or some such, as if it doesn't
>> >exist?  Disabling the WBA doesn't seem to do this.
>> 
>> You need to disable the WSX entry as well.  Unfortunately (due to a bug)
>> I think the only way you can do this is to edit xitami.cfg, and comment
>> out the line:
>> 
>>     admin=xiadmin
>
>[Wsx]
>  admin=""
>
>works for me in defaults.cfg. 

What this says is 'there is a /admin, and it is handled by the "" module', 
which is why you get the 501.  To completely hide the URL, so there is 
no /admin, you need to comment out the line in xitami.cfg instead, and
then you should get the 404.

If you can live with the 501, then your entry in defaults.cfg is tidier,
and less likely to break next time you upgrade xitami.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

>You are right that smthttpl.c:http_list_directory() is what is creating

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 10 18:49:14 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Tony Wenzelhuemer)
Date: Mon, 10 Dec 2001 19:49:14 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] PHP Nuke and others
In-Reply-To: <NEBBLGOJIKOELEDFHCCAAEMADJAA.jhadfiel@oldihc.org>
References: <20011210085433.91AE.SCOTT@therubberroom.org>
Message-ID: <5.1.0.14.2.20011210193754.00aa7c80@pop.chello.at>

Hi, i've sucessfully installed an run phpnuke( more exactly postnuke v.064) 
with xitami on win2k.

What you most probably get is WARNINGS _NOT ERRORS. This is php-related and 
occurs only due to sloppy php syntax (usage of single quotes instead of 
double quotes).
Try setting your php.ini settings to something like show_errors = ERRORS 
instead of ALL and most of them will vanish.

There is one problem with redirects in case you don't install your project 
into the (webserver) root directory, which you most likely want to do. To 
fix this I've submitted a fix to the postnuke project site somwhere at 
sourceforge.

Of course there are some minor bugs, it's still in development, but I 
consider it to be a way cool tool and suggest to give it a more thorough try.

tony

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Dec 12 13:05:29 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Wed, 12 Dec 2001 14:05:29 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] Emulating Apache directories
References: <200112100624.TAA31826@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>
Message-ID: <3C175619.3010609@freesbee.fr>

Ewen McNeill wrote:

>You are right that smthttpl.c:http_list_directory() is what is creating
>the directory (as an XML tree).  One of the things that it should also
>add to the XML is the path to the actual directory on disk, since it
>obviously needs to know this while it is preparing the list of files,
>and it would be useful to the GSL script outputting the directory.  The
>directory path is, I think, in p_http-> file_name, so adding an
>attribute with that value into the top level of the XML would be useful,
>called perhaps "path_on_disk".
>
>Ewen
>
OK so I inserted 2 lines at line 2113.

Old code
    /*  Create root XML 
item                                                 */
    root_item = xml_new (NULL, "directory", "");
   
    /*  Now transform directory listing into an XML 
tree                     */
    total_files = 0;
    total_size  = 0;

New code
    /*  Create root XML 
item                                                 */
    root_item = xml_new (NULL, "directory", "");
    /*  Output path to directory for GSL scripts */
    xml_put_attr (root_item, "physical_path", p_http-> file_name);
   
    /*  Now transform directory listing into an XML 
tree                     */
    total_files = 0;
    total_size  = 0;

This works fine and allows GSL directory scripts to search for README or 
similar.

It doesn't matter but it is important to note that you will not get the 
absoluet path of non-aliased directories, just the directory relative to 
the xitami base directory. I.e. you get webpage/images/ for the images 
directory in a default config. Since GSL doesn't seem to have a command 
to list the current working directory (e.g. /usr/local/xitami or 
/opt/xitami) you cannot infer from this variable where the xitami server 
is located on the file system. This seems to me to be excellent security 
as I can't see why you would need it but it should be noted for future 
reference.

However in testing this it seems that you cannot have an alias like 
relative = ../relative/ whereas rel = ./rel does work and the directory 
given for GSL is rel/

This could possibly be another bug?

Francis

-- 
"Education is when you read the fine print; 
  experience is what you get when you don't." Pete Seeger

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Dec 15 07:24:22 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (John Jonas)
Date: Sat, 15 Dec 2001 01:24:22 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] Robustness?
References: <3C1AF05E.7ABF9FA8@wayback.net>
Message-ID: <3C1AFAA6.B9340552@arbor-freight.com>

By far your weakest link is the dsl(128 up).  We ran over a year with a dual
channel ISDN for the same 128 up on a Pentium Pro 200mhz and 256mb ram.
Xitami is very processor and memory friendly.

Your low bandwidth is the stumbling block, but as long as you keep the
graphics down to under 50k per page and don't use any audio, video, flash et
cetera, you can serve quite a number of concurrent users.

Michael Wheeler wrote:

> graphics, no cgis or anything fancy.  The server will run on a dedicated
> computer connected to the internet by dsl (128 up).  I have a pentium II
> 333mhz with 320mb ram for the purpose.  My question is: what level of
> traffic should this system be able to handle and what is the weakest
> link - bandwidth, processor speed or memory?  I don't want to commit to
> this approach if the system will not be robust enough to handle several
> concurrent users.


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Dec 15 07:30:22 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Sat, 15 Dec 2001 02:30:22 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Robustness?
References: <3C1AF05E.7ABF9FA8@wayback.net>
Message-ID: <3C1AFC0E.31B1E595@rci.rutgers.edu>

With that rig, you may be limited by your 128K wire. But if you
are just serving basic pages, I think both your wire and your CPU
are over-kill. 

I had Xitami running on a 386SX-16 w/4 Megs. Single surfers
outside the building could NOT tell that it was a very lame
server; some commented that it seemed fast. Inside the building I
could feel a slight hesitation compared to my Pentium server  but
not much. 

Your P-333 is 40 times the power of that 386SX-16. 

When my main server was P-133 with 32 Megs RAM, one web-page
suddenly "took off". Up to 300 hits per day on a page with 27
images and a counter, on top of 200+ hits per day on the main
pages. (The "hot page" had an image of a woman in a shirt open to
her navel, but "nothing showing".... go figure.)

While I did not do a detailed analysis of the logs, I'm sure
there were simultaneous surfers. It held up just fine. When I
happened to be watching the CPU Utilization meter, it generally
sat at 2% with 1-second bursts that were higher, no sustained CPU
load. 

Likewise, even with 32M, the hard drive sat quietly, most data
cached in RAM. So quiet that when someone was sitting next to it
and I remotely started sucking the whole website down for
back-up, that person commented on the unusual racket. 

I've since moved it to a P-350 and 128M, and added Streaming
Media server to it, and that is fine and snappy even with many
hits a day. 

OK, here's my main server's stats at this moment: 

 HTTP service started at 20/Sep/2001 (*)
 Highest open connections:  25
 Total number of hits:  170260
 Total data transferred  2215Mb

(*) Last re-boot after move to new hardware... For a Windows App,
Xitami is mighty robust!

In your situation, I'd worry about the DSL. Is it really 24/7, or
more like 23.9/6.9 ? In my situation, hard-wired on the campus of
a large university, most of my server "outages" have not been my
server but the campus network. Router malfunction, 4 hours; DoS
storm, 2 days; and the power was out for a week while they
upgraded power transformers. You may be better served by a
commercial host, which should have better control of their link
to the Internet and their power needs. But, do-it-yourself can
work fine too. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Dec 15 07:59:02 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sat, 15 Dec 2001 20:59:02 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] SSI
In-Reply-To: Message from Joe@byrneworld.com
 of "Sat, 15 Dec 2001 01:45:07 MDT." <008101c1853c$80b63000$f6fea8c0@jjb>
Message-ID: <200112150759.UAA08412@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <008101c1853c$80b63000$f6fea8c0@jjb>, Joe@byrneworld.com writes:
>"Paul Reid" <preid@rci.rutgers.edu> writes:
>>> <!--#exec cgi="http://www.byrneworld.com/cgi-bin/ezcount.exe"-->
>>
>> Doesn't the EXEC function have to point to a Local path, rather
>> than a URL? Something like "C:\Xitami\cgi-bin\excount.exe" ?

If it's a "cgi" then it should be "/cgi-bin/CGINAME"; ie, it should be a
relative URL not a full URL.  This is particularly necessary with Xitami
2.4 and the PerlSSI, which takes a fairly naive approach to resolving
the path (stick the CGI directory name in front of CGINAME and hope for
the best).

If you're having trouble make sure you've got execution of CGIs turned
on, and check cgierr.log for any errors running the CGI.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

hello world


FYI: instead of using server side includes, you can also add a
<script src=http://www.server.com/cgi-bin/ezcount.exe></script>
The only difference in the exe file (compared to a exe-file that creates a 
complete page) is that the browser expects javascript, not html. Simply 
put: if you want to display "hello world" you will have to output 
"document.write('hello world');" [doubles quotes added for clarity].
I use a subroutine to add the javascript container to the desired output.

Marc

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Dec 15 19:07:53 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Sat, 15 Dec 2001 14:07:53 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] SSI
References: <006701c18531$f361a900$f6fea8c0@jjb>
Message-ID: <3C1B9F89.F2E19B51@rci.rutgers.edu>

> I want to create a drop down list in a form from items in a database.  I can code the CGI portion (i.e. grab the data out of the database and format the proper form code for the drop-down menu) but I can't quite make the final link to get the .SSI page to include this part.

SSI seems like a good idea but I notice that almost nobody uses
it. Needs grow until you reach a point that SSI either can't do
the job or the overhead chokes your CPU. 

Don't forget you can put the cart before the horse. Instead of a
static page that calls a program, you can call a program that
outputs static text with dynamic inserts. A half-way trick is to
use a Filter. 

I have a filter that reads static HTML and looks for magic tags.
When it finds a magic tag it grabs the parameter, looks for a
matching tag in a database, and inserts the data. That lets me
change a professor's biography and phone number one place and
have it appear on many pages. 

PHP is great for this kind of stuff (I shudda done it that way). 

You can also call a program in cgi-bin that outputs the whole
page, a mix of static and dynamic. The static can be hard-coded
but obviously it may be easier to maintain if it pulls the static
text from a template file (so the HTML maintainer does not step
on any C/Perl/VB code and break it). 

Most on-line ordering systems seem to directly call a cgi-bin EXE
or equivalent. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Dec 15 19:08:18 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)

Back to basics. VERY important: Xitami 2.4 or 2.5 ? 

The SSI handler changed radically between 2.4 and 2.5. 

In 2.4 it was an external Perl script. You need Perl, installed
and working. You can read through the Perl script (it is quite
simple) and see where it may be going astray.  

2.5 is officially "beta" so I have not even peeked at it. (I
drive 20 year old cars so I'm not one to jump on every new
model.) From comments here, 2.5 itself seems as stable as 2.4,
but some frills aren't done yet. In 2.5 the SSI is handled in the
main Xitami code. Apparently nobody uses SSI because I have not
seen much about it here. Again the source code (except in C) is
available for study. 

> the resulting page shows [xitami SSI:]  (the error code format as defined in the SSI page on xitami's configuration page) but I don't know what the error is

What exactly do you see? If you actually see "the error code
format" rather than an error code, my blind-guess is that the C
routine can't find Perl. 

I'm confused by Ewen's comments and will post to him. 

Marc's idea to use a SCRIPT tag may be off the mark. That would
seem to run on the Browser, not the Server. For a "Hello world",
that might be cool, except a Win32 EXE won't work on Mac or unix,
and Win-users may object to running your (possibly malicious)
code on their machine (I don't think any Win browser actually
will run an EXE as a SCRIPT). For a counter, it is no good
because the count has to be kept on your server, not on hundreds
of browsers. If you "want to create a drop down list in a form
from items in a database" on your server, obviously the EXE has
to run on your server (or have some magic way to run on the
client while accessing your server database, which is really
doing it the hard way). 

 -PRR

>> If it's a "cgi" then it should be "/cgi-bin/CGINAME"; ie, it should be a 
>> relative URL not a full URL. This is particularly necessary with Xitami 2.4 
>> and the PerlSSI, which takes a fairly naive approach to resolving the

>> best).
>
>Then if PerlSSI "blindly" sticks the CGI directory in front of
>the CGINAME, shouldn't it be "CGINAME" rather than "/cgi-bin/CGINAME"? 

No.  The "/cgi-bin" is stripped off, and then the CGI-BIN directory is
placed in front of what remains.  Looking at the way it is stripped off,
it _might_ work with a full URL, coincidentallly, if the URL names the
same site, but I'm not sure that's particularly portable.

Ewen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Dec 16 09:02:05 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marc Doigny)
Date: Sun, 16 Dec 2001 10:02:05 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] SSI
In-Reply-To: <3C1B9FA2.29CC01FA@rci.rutgers.edu>
References: <006701c18531$f361a900$f6fea8c0@jjb>
Message-ID: <5.0.2.1.2.20011216094207.00a313e0@190.190.190.1>


>Marc's idea to use a SCRIPT tag may be off the mark. That would
>seem to run on the Browser, not the Server. For a "Hello world",
>that might be cool, except a Win32 EXE won't work on Mac or unix,

The first (and most normal) use of the script is for placing javascript on 
the page.
The browser expects that what it reads from the file is javascript.
It's like an <img src= ...> tag, but instead of loading an image, it loads 
javascript code.

I use lots of <script src= ...> for including logo's, footers and so on on 
my pages.
When something changes, i only have to modify one sigle script and all the 
pages calling that script are modified accordingly. It's like CCS 
(Cascading Style Sheets).
For instance, place following code on a html page and look for the results:
<script src=http://www.idemdito.org/mailing.js></script>

Now the fine thing about it, is that the browser expects javascript code, 
whatever the extension is. If you call <script 
src="http://web.verfaillie.com/cgi-bin/c"></script>, Xitami will execute 
the code (AND NOT SEND IT TO THE BROWSER) and send the results to the client.

The only minus is that it takes longer to process a <script> (when the 
script is called for the first time) than a SSI because the script code has 
to be fetched from the server. For the subsequent calls, the browser cache 
is used.


>and Win-users may object to running your (possibly malicious)
>code on their machine (I don't think any Win browser actually
>will run an EXE as a SCRIPT).

Xitami won't send the code to the clients if the code resides in the 
cgi-bin derectory.


Marc

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Dec 16 19:57:02 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Mon, 17 Dec 2001 08:57:02 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Admin Area Rename
In-Reply-To: Message from "Pablo" <phpshop@phpshop.org>
 of "Thu, 13 Dec 2001 21:07:58 CDT." <EIEFKMGPDJCOPNFNDKIACEGODCAA.phpshop@phpshop.org>
Message-ID: <200112161957.IAA29249@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <EIEFKMGPDJCOPNFNDKIACEGODCAA.phpshop@phpshop.org>, "Pablo" writes:
>I have a site that has a directory called "Admin" just off the root
>directory.  I try to access it and I get the xitami admin login prompt!  How
>do I rename the admin area path to something else?  

You _should_ be able to rename this by editing xitami.cfg, in the [WSX]
section, and changing the "admin=xiadmin" entry to something else, eg
"xitamiadmin=xiadmin".  I'm not certain that everything there is set up
so that it can be renamed, but if you remove that entry then it should
be completely gone.

Note: you'll have to edit xitami.cfg (which we don't usually recommend),
rather than trying to override it in defaults.cfg; there is a bug
reported for this (ie, that it should be possible to disabled WSXes in
defaults.cfg)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 17 17:28:57 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Mon, 17 Dec 2001 12:28:57 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] SSI
References: <200112150759.UAA08412@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz> <3C1BA07E.E901ADE3@rci.rutgers.edu> <009101c185a1$55a7e560$f6fea8c0@jjb>
Message-ID: <3C1E2B59.85695F6F@rci.rutgers.edu>

> I don't do PERL, PHP, or other scripting language...to me that would be taking big steps backwards, 

Why? Perl was made for extracting info from databases and formatting it
for text printers (or files or streams). PHP is like Perl embedded in
HTML. 

If it is a matter of not abandoning the EXEs you have already built: use
PHP to build most of the page as HTML and use the PHP function to call
an EXEcutable where you already have a tool. 

Getting back to your concept: in X2.4 there is a test-file TESTSSI.SSI.
You need Perl for the SSI feature to work in X2.4. On my WinNT server,
this line works fine: 

Output of CGI program: 
 <!--#exec cgi="/cgi-bin/testcgi.exe?arguments"--><BR>

On my machine: 
 TESTSSI.SSI is in C:\Webpages
 Testcgi.exe is in C:\Xitami\cgi-bin

Testcgi is an EXE program supplied by Xitami that simply prints some
environment variables as HTML. 

> Your filter idea is really intriguing

So try it. Put a copy of DOS SORT.EXE in \Xitami\cgi-bin. Write a HTML
file that prints several different lines of text, and call it TEST.SRT
and put it in your web folder.  

In defaults.cfg, add a line to tell Xitami what to do with an SRT file
(feed it to SORT): 
   [Filter]
    .SRT=c:\xitami\cgi-bin\sort.exe
    .ssi=c:\xitami\perlssi

In a browser, open localhost\TEST.SRT. Xitami should feed the file to
SORT and send it to your browser. The output will be a Mess, because
your browser will be baffled by out-of-order HTML tags and will probably
re-wrap lines. But you should see that your multi-line text comes back
alphabetized by the first character on each line.

If you like making EXEs.... write one that reads Standard In, replaces
all occurrences of "Large" with "Colossal!!!", and writes to Standard
Out. Write a HTML file with the word "Large" in it, save it in your web
folder with a unique file extension. Set Xitami's filter configuration
to feed that extension to your EXE in cgi-bin. Open that file through
the server and see that all your "Large" products are now "Colossal!!!" 

The next step, replacing some unique string or tag with data from
elsewhere, is left as an exercise.  

> Win32 executables.  This offers tremendous power for me, but making
small changes to an otherwise static page can be a big job.  

That's a good summary. However Perl/PHP come with functions directly
aimed at database reporting and text formatting, are typically far
easier to change than an EXE, and can call an EXE if that is the best
way to do it. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 17 19:40:43 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Tue, 18 Dec 2001 08:40:43 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Multiple ports
In-Reply-To: Message from "Frank Harrell" <frank@nps-vip.net>
 of "Mon, 17 Dec 2001 08:26:58 CDT." <000001c186fe$81238b50$6400a8c0@COWBOY>
Message-ID: <200112171940.IAA04081@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <000001c186fe$81238b50$6400a8c0@COWBOY>, "Frank Harrell" writes:
>Howdy, Does anyone know if it is possible to have Xitami listen on 2
>ports (80 & 443) at the same time? 

No, Xitami can't do this (listen on two ports at once).  (It'd be handy, 
but it can't at present.)

BTW, Xitami/Pro will list on port 80 (http) and port 443 (https) at
once, since it supports SSL.  Xitami itself doesn't support SSL though;
it's a feature only in the Pro version.

The typically solution to listening on two ports at once is to run two
copies of Xitami.  Providing they're in different directories, and have
all the other services disabled/moved to different ports (FTP, LRWP,
etc) they should work together.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Dec 18 20:12:14 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Wed, 19 Dec 2001 09:12:14 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] Directory Listing
In-Reply-To: Message from "Jason Ozin at Technica Solutions" <jason@tec1.co.uk>

Message-ID: <200112182012.JAA06570@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <001501c187f7$bdea3800$1564a8c0@troy.ozin.foo>, "Jason Ozin at Techni
ca Solutions" writes:
>Prior to v2.4d9 I was using the non-service version. Something that seems to
>have changed is that Dir-script = seems to be completely ignored now. You
>can't assign a template and  you can't use graphics in directory listings.
>Is this a bug or by design? 

As far as I know the Dir-script option was only in the Xitami 2.5 beta
(which includes GSL).  It won't work in Xitami 2.4, because the GSL
support wasn't introduced until the 2.5 development version.  In Xitami
2.4 the directory listings that are generated are hard coded.  You could
perhaps use PHP or similar instead if you want to customise things (ie,
have your own index pages).

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Subject: [Xitami] How to protect a cgi-bin subdirectory?
References: <001801c187e7$5ae70810$0203a8c0@cartman>
Message-ID: <000f01c18880$b751b020$659305c3@futeltra>

running same version I am able to do this for sure
perhaps you need no quotes surrounding password
i have something like this

[/cgi-bin/subfolder]
    username1=password1
    username2=password2
    ..... etc.
I have a lot of 20+ users on this folder everithing works fine.

Also be sure to edit the right .aut file
If you use defaults.aut then make sure your config (xitami.cfg or
defaults.cfg) points to this file but not some other
[Security]
    filename=defaults.aut

| Version: 2.5b5
|

| the scripts
| in there.  Adding the following:
|    [/cgi-bin/music]
|          friendly = "users"
|
| To defaults.aut does not do it. I am not prompted for a password when
runing
| those scripts.


From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Dec 19 12:13:18 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)

Michael Pierce wrote:

>Version: 2.5b5
>
>I'm trying to figure our how to password protect a sub directory of cgi-bin.
>For example,
>I want "/cgi-bin/music" to be protected so that only trusted users can run
>the scripts

>   [/cgi-bin/music]
>         friendly = "users"
>
>To defaults.aut does not do it. I am not prompted for a password when runing
>those scripts.

Another of these annoying 'it works for me' people I'm afraid

In my defaults.cfg I have (amongst other things)
[Security]
    Filename = "defaults.aut"

And in defaults.aut I have (amongst other things)
[/cgi-bin/exec]
    user = "password"

Works on 2.5b5 both as localhost and to a remote server

You can even add the Webmask = <ipaddresslist> line if you want to only 
let certain scripts be run by known IP addresses. One thing I have 
noticed is that browsers often remain 'logged in' for a long time so you 
can only retest by closing the browser and restarting then you get the 
login prompt.

Francis

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Wed Dec 19 17:32:47 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Francis Turner)
Date: Wed, 19 Dec 2001 18:32:47 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] BUG - uppercase subdirs of an Alias - potenial NULL pointer assignemnt
Message-ID: <3C20CF3F.6000500@freesbee.fr>

Just found a lovely bug.

I have (for test purposes!) within my defaults.cfg an alias line
usrlocal = "/usr/local"

(Xitami is installed and runing in /usr/local/xitami-25b5)

I also have a subdirectory from /usr/local/xitami-25b5/webpages called 
UPPERCASE

http://computer/UPPERCASE/ works and returns the directory contents
http://computer/usrlocal/xitami-25b5/webpages/ works and gives the home page
http://computer/usrlocal/xitami-25b5/webpages/UPPERCASE/ gives a 404

The same applies to ftp aliases since they also call the same routine 
(see below)! but if ftproot is set to /usr/local/ for a user then that 
user can go to ftp://computer/xitami-25b5/webpages/UPPERCASE/ just fine

It looks like this is because the http_match_alias () routine in 
smthttpd.c lowercases the buffer for comparison and then returns as the 
 value of char **base the lowercased remainder of the url not the 
equivalent untoughed raminder of the url.

I think the fix would be to keep track of the offset and return that 
instead which means that base would have to be changed from a char** to 
an int *. Alternatively you could set base to &uri[slash-buffer] 
(??should be &uri[slash-buffer-1] if the leading / is absent??)

In looking at this code I think I also see a potential null pointer 
assignment (I think it never actually occurs because this routine is 
always called with a parameter for base) but there seems to be no check 
to see whetehr base == NULL before assigning *base to buffer at line 832 
although there is such a check for line 851

Francis

-- 
...if the US Government were ever to get really serious about Internet 
security, the top players in Microsoft's management hierarchy would find 
themselves handcuffed, blindfolded, led onto a tarmac within some obscure 
Air Force base, and shot.
-- Thomas C Greene (http://www.theregister.co.uk/content/55/23223.html)

Forgot to mention the workaround : Add a link by "ln -s path alias" in 
the webpages directory.

Note this could lead to infitte recursion down directory trees if not 
careful and it does so in the toy example I just used above

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Dec 20 06:58:03 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Thu, 20 Dec 2001 19:58:03 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] CHMOD in cgi-bin doesn't work
In-Reply-To: Message from "Steve Cox" <aptsales@mweb.co.za>
 of "Thu, 20 Dec 2001 08:07:03 +0200." <005101c1891c$91df3aa0$4abefea9@f2k7o6>
Message-ID: <200112200658.TAA16818@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <005101c1891c$91df3aa0$4abefea9@f2k7o6>, "Steve Cox" writes:
>I connect with my FTP client to 127.0.0.1 as admin with all rights, if I try
>to chmod my perl cgi file in the cgi-bin permissions to 755 for example I
>get the error message: "502 'SITE' not implemented ! chmod failed. 

chmod, etc, are not implemented in Xitami's FTP server -- it's a fairly
basic FTP server intended for anonymous-FTP and some basic webpage
uploads.

If you need more advanced features I suggest you disable Xitami's FTP
server and install another one with the extra features you need.

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Content-Type: text/plain; charset="us-ascii"; format=flowed

At 12:27 18/12/01, you wrote:
>Using win2k+xitami25.5b4
>I'm trying to execute an .exe script (<form action="cgi.exe">), but it 
>keeps giving the script to  a download manager. What to do?
>II am the administrator of this computer and I have rights to execute that 
>script. I heard that xitami doesn't necessarily run the script in the same 
>directory and with the same rights.

Only scripts in some directories are treated as scripts and executed 
locally on the server. Anything else is send to the browser client.
Your script should look at the environment so it can find the output file.
and read your windows manual for topics on execute rights (i'm only working 
with w'98)


Marc

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Dec 21 18:03:50 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)
Date: Fri, 21 Dec 2001 13:03:50 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami And PHP
In-Reply-To: <013001c18a45$86e49b70$5e01a8c0@brian>
Message-ID: <002b01c18a49$d8031190$0100a8c0@celeron2k>

    I've had a somewhat similar problem regarding caching. I fixed it in my
case by generating an extra HTTP header, from my PHP source, like this:

header ("Cache-Control: no-store, no-cache, must-revalidate, post-check=0,
pre-check=0");


	I've also has a similar problem regarding PHP_SELF and portability across
Xitami and Apache. In my case I did this:

// Under Apache $PHP_SELF is what we want, under Xitami it is $SCRIPT_NAME
// We find out based on which one has ".php" in it.
if (ereg ("\.php", $SCRIPT_NAME)) $GLOBAL_SELF = $SCRIPT_NAME;
else $GLOBAL_SELF = $PHP_SELF;
$GLOBAL_SELF = str_replace ("\\\\", "/", $GLOBAL_SELF);

	and then I use $GLOBAL_SELF

	Hope it helps

marcio

Sent: December 21, 2001 12:33 PM
To: Xitami@lists.xitami.org
Subject: [Xitami] Xitami And PHP


I'm having a slight problem getting this to run properly.  I've set the
filter's up, .php = source of php.exe, and have the latest version of php
4.1.0

My problem is this, I have a "Picture Gallery" page written in php that you
can upload images to, and it is supposed to show these images in the image
index upon a succesful upload.  I've tested this script on IIS 5.0 and it
was working fine.  Now when I run it, after the upload, it doesn't show the
image I just uploaded.  The only way to get the images to appear is to open
the script, edit it, say add a comment //a or something like that, save the
script, then refresh the browser.  It's almost as if Xitami is not allowing
php.exe to be recalled.  It's very strange behaviour and I've found no way
around it beyond my little edit the source code/refresh fixer.  Any ideas on
why it would be doing this?   Think it could possibly be the Xitami server?

I've also noticed that the $PHP_SELF function, doesn't call the
path/filename, the whole weblink + php script, it only calls the root
directory.  Here's an Example.

Say:   http://www.someplace.com/picture.php  is called.   Within picture.php
is a call to $PHP_SELF, which is just supposed to be the previous link.
This is not the case tho in Xitami, it ends up being
http://www.someplace.com/  without the picture.php  So I've had to edit a
lot of scripts to add the actual file name.  Not sure if this would be PHP
related, or Xitmai related, but I'd figured I'd mention that too.  Any
idea's on either of these issues would be greatly appreciated.

Thanks for your time,

~SandMan

----- Original Message -----
From: "Marcio Marchini" <mqm@magma.ca>
To: <xitami@lists.xitami.org>
Sent: Friday, December 21, 2001 1:03 PM
Subject: RE: [Xitami] Xitami And PHP


>
>     I've had a somewhat similar problem regarding caching. I fixed it in
my
> case by generating an extra HTTP header, from my PHP source, like this:
>
> header ("Cache-Control: no-store, no-cache, must-revalidate, post-check=0,
> pre-check=0");
>
>
> I've also has a similar problem regarding PHP_SELF and portability across
> Xitami and Apache. In my case I did this:
>
> // Under Apache $PHP_SELF is what we want, under Xitami it is $SCRIPT_NAME
> // We find out based on which one has ".php" in it.
> if (ereg ("\.php", $SCRIPT_NAME)) $GLOBAL_SELF = $SCRIPT_NAME;
> else $GLOBAL_SELF = $PHP_SELF;
> $GLOBAL_SELF = str_replace ("\\\\", "/", $GLOBAL_SELF);
>
> and then I use $GLOBAL_SELF
>
> Hope it helps
>
> marcio
>
>
> -----Original Message-----
> From: xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org
[mailto:xitami-admin@lists.xitami.org]On

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Dec 22 04:14:48 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Marcio Marchini)
Date: Fri, 21 Dec 2001 23:14:48 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Looking for a Chat script
In-Reply-To: <ulc72ugo4nat69pum8jt7c0bh155cc8j8l@4ax.com>
Message-ID: <000201c18a9f$31f90100$0100a8c0@celeron2k>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_0003_01C18A75.49260640
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit

  a.. Freechat http://www.sonic.net/~nbs/unix/www/freechat/
    a.. Con: Code (cgi-bins) in C, not in PHP - harder to change/customize
for your needs if required.

  a.. ARSC Really Simple Chat (http://freshmeat.net/projects/arsc/ )
    a.. Pro: PHP based.
    b.. Pro: Works on Mysql
    c.. Con: No name reservation, colors, instant messaging.
    d.. Overall: Does not have many features. Is a plain/simple chat.


  a.. PHP WEBCHAT http://www.csit-sun.pub.ro/~gygy/chat/
    a.. Con: Too simple, check the demo chatroom at the page above

  a.. WebChat http://www.webdev.ro/products/webchat/index.php
    a.. Con: Install failed to create database tables. "The used table type
doesn't support AUTO_INCREMENT columns"

  a.. MWChat http://freshmeat.net/projects/mwchat/ (demo at
http://www.appindex.net/applications/development_releases/mwchat/demo/ )
    a.. Con: Download is a beta. Expires after 1 week, wants to send email
do devel.
    b.. Con: Could not get it to work
    c.. Con: MWChat is copyrighted 2000-2001 Appindex.Net
  a.. phpMyChat http://www.phpheaven.net/
    a.. Pro: Very nice install, web-based, worked just fine
    b.. Pro: Supports custom colors, smilies, etc.
    c.. Pro: Works on MySQL, PostgreSQL or ODBC
    d.. Pro: Fairly nice GUI
    e.. Pro: In PHP, easier to change if needed
    f.. Con: Can't associate pictures with users, as far as I know

  a.. phpWebChat http://chat.nitco.com/
    a.. Con: Does not work under my test setup: Warning: crypt() is not
supported in this PHP build in C:/Xitami/webpages/phpchat/engine/room.php on
line 22
    b.. Con: Last update: 7/27/00

  a.. PHPOpenChat http://www.ortelius.de/phpopenchat/
    a.. Con: PHP safe_mode has to be set to Off. "Explanation: If the safe
mode are enabled we can't change php.ini variables during chat's runtime and
that is what we need in output.php, a script which never ends."
    b.. Con: Does not work under my test setup: Warning: crypt() is not
supported in this PHP build in
C:\Xitami\webpages\openchat\includes\check_permissions_inc.php on line 35

  a.. TAHC http://freshmeat.net/projects/tahc/
    a.. Con: GUI, didn't like it. See demo at
http://www.itcampus.dk/tahc/tahc.php . Haven't tried installing it because
of that.

  a.. PHProjekt
    a.. Pro: It is much more than just Chat, it is a full suite. More
integrated with the rest, same look-and-feel, nice to have something like
MyYahoo
    b.. Pro: Setup of this tool is a breeze. Web-based, it all just worked !
    c.. Con: The chat app flickers when it refreshes (background color
problem ?)
    d.. Con: No smilies or custom colors in chat

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Dec 22 22:59:13 2001

Subject: [Xitami] FTP log
Message-ID: <200112222306.AAA27731@sxpublic.nxrda.imatix.net>

The FTP log is maintained in the access log, same with HTTP. I believe FTP errors are in the errors.log.
Do an FTP to your site, then check the access log. You'll see your actions.

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)

> This access log looks like a collection of hack attempts.

Since you didn't post a snippet, we must guess what you are
seeing.

However, for the last few months, 95% of my errors.log and much
of my access.log is CodeRed, Nimba, or hack-scripts. 

> Alot of calls to WINNT directory. Funny I don't have WINNT

It is quicker for scripters to just try to access it than to
figure out what O/S you are on. That (invalid) URL will produce
no response or a 404 on most machines, but un-patched infected MS
IIS webserver will give a response (typically DIR). Hackers can
grep the script's output and quickly gleen a list of machines
worthy of further attention. 

 -PRR

In-Reply-To: Message from Bruce <bd4u@earthlink.net>

In message <4v2b2ucergmms44s2ngqrb40l25cgff8sv@4ax.com>, Bruce writes:
>What does PHP stand for?

IIRC originally "Personal Home Pages".  It's a scripting language.

See http://www.php.net./

It's evolved a lot since its "Personal Home Pages" origin.  The current
"official" expansion appears to be "PHP: Hypertext Preprocessor" (which
is a recursive acronym).

It's got nothing much to do with perl, although some of the syntax is
the same.

>Does it support WIN/95, any chance of a 16 bit version? 

There is a version for Windows, which ought to work on Windows 95 AFAIK.
There's almost certainly not a 16-bit version though -- 16-bit Windows
is _very_ old (7-8 years now), and not much is still supporting it.

Ewen

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Dec 23 08:23:39 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 23 Dec 2001 21:23:39 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] FTP log
In-Reply-To: Message from Bruce <bd4u@earthlink.net>
 of "Sat, 22 Dec 2001 00:36:05 CDT." <nf682uc4pk2u73j59vf6hqo4il67fdeb42@4ax.com>
Message-ID: <200112230823.VAA13636@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <nf682uc4pk2u73j59vf6hqo4il67fdeb42@4ax.com>, Bruce writes:
>Is there an FTP log somewhere in Xitami that will tell me which files 
>are being transfered from \ftproot\pub and when?

These are recorded in the same log as the HTTP transfers -- as far as
Xitami is concerned, it's all just files :-)

>What would be a good way to collect, store, and delete old log files in 
>Xitami. 

You can configure Xitami to rotate the log files daily (weekly/monthly),
and save them.  Then you can have an external program process them into
pretty reports (analog, webalizer, webtrends, et al), and something else
archive them later.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Dec 23 08:13:07 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Control-Freak)
Date: Sun, 23 Dec 2001 03:13:07 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] lots of good replies..
References: <4v2b2ucergmms44s2ngqrb40l25cgff8sv@4ax.com>
Message-ID: <002901c18b89$a7792780$b61e2341@concentric.net>

Well, don't let the name fool you.  It actually stands for Personal Home
Page.  It was originally intended to be a simple cut down version of perl so
that home page users could put some scripting into their regular html pages.
But, the implementation of it grew in popularity over the years, and
webmasters started using it.  Since it was open source, it was contributed
to quickly. And, some will argue that it is at least as powerful as Perl
itself if not more now.

At least that is what my SAMs book says about it.

Jay Aldrich

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Dec 23 22:12:53 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (evan heller)
Date: Sun, 23 Dec 2001 17:12:53 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] What is iHTML????
References: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCEEIBCEAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
Message-ID: <3C2656E5.513581D0@alum.rpi.edu>

iHTML used to be called MivaMia and is very similar to cgi scripting. I'm
fairly sure you can get it to work with xitami (I did it back in the day when
it was called by its original name), however, iHTML is not well supported
everywhere as a programming language. There are plenty of other languages out
there that work like iHTML (but better supported) for example: C or Perl CGI
scripting, JSP, PHP,ASP, Python and ColdFusion.

-Evan

Hello

You should be lucky you are using Xitami and not a microsoft server.
There are attempts by virusses to get information out of your computer or 
to run programs on your server.
Since the virusses target microsoft windows servers and these servers 
mostly use win nt, the virusses are trying to get access to the windows nt 
system directory.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 24 17:02:09 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Hugo Notti)
Date: Mon, 24 Dec 2001 18:02:09 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] lots of good replies..
References: <4v2b2ucergmms44s2ngqrb40l25cgff8sv@4ax.com>
Message-ID: <002001c18c9c$ba65dff0$0201a8c0@dieter>

PHP is just another programming language for CGI.

PHP code is written directly into the HTML code, parsed by the server and
then replaced by the output of the program.

One strength of PHP seems to be database interaction.

Same as Perl, PHP is a scripting language that is not compiled.

PHP is available for all major (and many minor) Servers and operating
systems.

As far as I know PHP has been developed especially for CGI tasks and has
many built in commands for these - unlike other programming languages such
as Perl, C, etc., where you need libraries, modules or individual hard
coding.

Why don't you download PHP, install it and see for yourself? There are very
good tutorials in the web. When downloading, you will find out if there is a
16-bit version too. The official website is http://www.php.net/.

Good luck,

Hugo

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Dec 25 03:27:40 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Hugo Notti)
Date: Tue, 25 Dec 2001 04:27:40 +0100
Subject: [Xitami] lots of good replies..
References: <NDBBIDKBILPOMBMKDOOCMEIDCEAA.alsiman@cofs.net>
Message-ID: <000401c18cf4$1ccb5100$0201a8c0@dieter>

What do you mean by "...something fancier than CGI forms..."?

While Javascript is (in almost all cases) executed inside the browser
(client side), PHP is executed on the server (server side). So the browser
"talks" to the server in Javascript and the server "replies" in PHP (which
is a somewhat misleading description because the server only returns HTML
code which has been generated by parsing the PHP upon the browsers request
generated by Javascript on in another way).
Inside a document, PHP and Javascript are distinguishable by their enclosing
tags. So they can both, coexist and interact. It works as well (or even
better) as communication by a mixture of letters, email, fax, phone and
personal meetings.

Go to www.php.net and read the tutorial for beginners. This will help you
much more because then you can actually see PHP.

Good luck,

Hugo

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Tue Dec 25 23:22:41 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (xitami@lists.xitami.org)
Date: Tue, 25 Dec 2001 17:22:41 -0600
Subject: [Xitami] (no subject)
References: <20011225175127.71272.qmail@web11308.mail.yahoo.com> <009d01c18d80$8cd7ae80$f6fea8c0@jjb> <OE61Cl9FopYC98Bi89Q00003ce6@hotmail.com>
Message-ID: <00cb01c18d9b$0e462590$f6fea8c0@jjb>

Peter (and Bruce)
     The thing that brought me to Xitami first was the easy way it handled
multiple domains.  I sell DSL service and had to offer web hosting to be
competitive.  Xitami was a perfect fit, especially for the price!  The
easiest way to create a virtual host is by using the VHost Wizard from the
main menu of the Web Based Administor (http://localhost/admin).  Looking at
the VHost configuration page:

1. Virtual host profile: (The configuration file created for all custom
settings for this domain).  I use the top level domain name less the
extension. (ie. for imatix.com I would use imatix).  The extension .cfg is
automatically used.

2.  Over-write existing file:  There usually isn't one, but if there is,
check this to replace the old configuration file.

3.  Select IP Address:  If you have multiple NICs and you only want one for
Web hosting, select it here, otherwise (default) let Xitami use "All" IP
addresses.

4.  Or DNS Host Name.  Enter the Web address here, ie: www.yourdomain.com

5.  Web Page root directory:  The location on your drive where the web site
pages are stored.  This is the directory where your customer has FTP access
to update page in.

6.  cgi-bin directory:  I usually cut-n-paste the directory above and add
\cgi-bin to it.  You can point this to any directory where you want where
cgi scripts for this domain are allowed to run.

7.  FTP root directory:  I don't use Xitami's FTP server, but I assume this
is the "home" directory for the admin of this domain.  (same as #5 I would
guess)

The rest of the items are pretty self explanatory.  I usually let Xitami
create the above directories for me.  Once you save it, you need to restart
the server and your all set!  The DNS entries for the domain only needs to
have a CNAME or A record for www.yurdoamin.com (which is normally a default)
that points to your public IP address.  My default, xitami will try to use a
page named 'default.htm' when no specific page name is specified on the
address line.  If that fails, it will look for index.htm.  You can change
and add to these in the VHost configuration screen.  If you look in the
xitami directory, you will find configuration files (and .aut security
files) for each host (domain).  These can be manually edited just like the
default file, or you can do all your maintenance through the web based
administration app.

Its all very easy, even though it looks complicated at first site.  Once you
get two domains running, you'll be off setting up web sites for all your
friends!  (just make sure you charge them something....xitami may be free,
but bandwidth isn't!!)

--Joe

>The rest of the items are pretty self explanatory.  I usually let Xitami
>create the above directories for me.  Once you save it, you need to restart
>the server and your all set!  The DNS entries for the domain only needs to
>have a CNAME or A record for www.yurdoamin.com (which is normally a default)
>that points to your public IP address.  My default, xitami will try to use a
>page named 'default.htm' when no specific page name is specified on the
>address line.  If that fails, it will look for index.htm.  You can change
>and add to these in the VHost configuration screen.  If you look in the
>xitami directory, you will find configuration files (and .aut security
>files) for each host (domain).  These can be manually edited just like the
>default file, or you can do all your maintenance through the web based
>administration app.
>
>Its all very easy, even though it looks complicated at first site.  Once you
>get two domains running, you'll be off setting up web sites for all your
>friends!  (just make sure you charge them something....xitami may be free,
>but bandwidth isn't!!)
>
>--Joe
>

On Tue, 25 Dec 2001 17:22:41 -0600, you wrote:

>Peter (and Bruce)
>     The thing that brought me to Xitami first was the easy way it handled
>multiple domains.  I sell DSL service and had to offer web hosting to be
>competitive.  Xitami was a perfect fit, especially for the price!  The
>easiest way to create a virtual host is by using the VHost Wizard from the
>main menu of the Web Based Administor (http://localhost/admin).  Looking at
>the VHost configuration page:
>
>1. Virtual host profile: (The configuration file created for all custom
>settings for this domain).  I use the top level domain name less the
>extension. (ie. for imatix.com I would use imatix).  The extension .cfg is
>automatically used.
>
>2.  Over-write existing file:  There usually isn't one, but if there is,
>check this to replace the old configuration file.
>
>3.  Select IP Address:  If you have multiple NICs and you only want one for
>Web hosting, select it here, otherwise (default) let Xitami use "All" IP
>addresses.
>
>4.  Or DNS Host Name.  Enter the Web address here, ie: www.yourdomain.com
>
>5.  Web Page root directory:  The location on your drive where the web site
>pages are stored.  This is the directory where your customer has FTP access
>to update page in.
>
>6.  cgi-bin directory:  I usually cut-n-paste the directory above and add
>\cgi-bin to it.  You can point this to any directory where you want where
>cgi scripts for this domain are allowed to run.
>
>7.  FTP root directory:  I don't use Xitami's FTP server, but I assume this
>is the "home" directory for the admin of this domain.  (same as #5 I would
>guess)
>
>The rest of the items are pretty self explanatory.  I usually let Xitami
>create the above directories for me.  Once you save it, you need to restart
>the server and your all set!  The DNS entries for the domain only needs to
>have a CNAME or A record for www.yurdoamin.com (which is normally a default)
>that points to your public IP address.  My default, xitami will try to use a
>page named 'default.htm' when no specific page name is specified on the
>address line.  If that fails, it will look for index.htm.  You can change
>and add to these in the VHost configuration screen.  If you look in the
>xitami directory, you will find configuration files (and .aut security
>files) for each host (domain).  These can be manually edited just like the
>default file, or you can do all your maintenance through the web based
>administration app.
>
>Its all very easy, even though it looks complicated at first site.  Once you
>get two domains running, you'll be off setting up web sites for all your
>friends!  (just make sure you charge them something....xitami may be free,
>but bandwidth isn't!!)
>
>--Joe
>

Bruce,
   Can't help you there.  I never liked the way xitami implemented FTP.  I'm
of the old school anyway....a program ought to do one thing, and do it very
well.  Web hosting and FTP are not in the same ballpark.  I have used SERV-U
FTP server for years.  The new version (I don't see any great improvement)
jumped way up in price, but all previous versions sold for $30.00.  Really
hard to beat.  You can do what you want, but for me, I'd rather have a
separate FTP server and not worry about mixing configurations.

--Joe

> I have the following problem using the web based administration on Xitami
> for Linux.  When I make setting changes via the web admin screens the
> settings do not stick.  If I manually modify the cgf files using the pico
> editor, the setting stick.  I'm using the save buttons, restarting the
> server, but no changes stay.


I remember having this same problem when first using Xitami. The solution,
in my case, was to click the Save icon (sometimes more than once if you are
on one of the sub-configuration pages) until the main Xitami Administration
page is displayed -- then click Restart Server. I found that clicking the
Restart icon on any of the configuration pages would lose the changes.

- Jeff
Xitami v2.4d9

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Thu Dec 27 19:44:09 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 28 Dec 2001 08:44:09 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] How to find user of port on linux?

Message-ID: <200112271944.IAA05728@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <200112271429125.SM00191@there>, Bob Paddock writes:
>I just buld Xitami on my Mandrake 8.1 linux box.
>When I try to start it up it tells me that port 80 and 81 are already in use, 
>which is news to me.  

If you're running a webserver on a linux system and want to use the
standard ports (80, etc), then you need to start the webserver as root
-- only root has the ability to open those ports. 

I suspect you'll find that's what's going on, rather than that there is
some other program using those ports.

Ewen

You Wrote :
>>So it sounds like something different is going on.
>>Can anyone else reproduce this issue on another version of Windows?
>>(There were bugs like this -- accessing a device in the "wrong" way

Response

With Windows, if installing, ununstalling and fiddling ... consider
a clean format of the drive and a fresh install with all known (by you)
to work device drivers.    

The build of the OS ... in particular those
builds that 'burn' the OS image onto the drive ... can make a big difference.

Your weird behaviour is an indication of a need to service pack the OS
or rebuild it fresh.

Always good to ChkDsk the hard drive on a crash and certainly ... delete your
temp files.

Win 95, 98 and ME are not ideal environments for servers. ( In particular when you got
the MP3 jamming)

I'd look at the OS.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Dec 28 08:04:52 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 28 Dec 2001 21:04:52 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] FTP problems
In-Reply-To: Message from Bruce Axtens <axtens_@mac.com>
 of "Fri, 28 Dec 2001 15:34:43 +0800." <5C6A0688-FB65-11D5-8692-0003933D8C18@mac.com>
Message-ID: <200112280804.VAA08868@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <5C6A0688-FB65-11D5-8692-0003933D8C18@mac.com>, Bruce Axtens writes:
>If I ftp from my iBook to my desktop, via ethernet crossover cable and 
>static non-routable class C addresses, no problem.
>But if I ftp from my iBook across the internet I can log on and chdir, 
>but I every time I try to NLST, it times out. I've tried 3 different ftp 
>clients to the same (non) effect.

Do you have a firewall in between the Internet and your Xitami server?  
It looks a whole lot like the data channel connection is being blocked
by your firewall.  You might want to try active mode FTP (there's a
slightly better chance of it working in the case of the FTP server being
behind a firewall); most programs default to passive mode these days
(because it's got a better chance of working when the _client_ is behind
a firewall).

(And yes, if both the client and server are behind different firewalls
it is quite possible for FTP to be completely broken, so that neither
passive or active FTP will work.  Don't use FTP.  Use HTTP.  It's much
cleaner.)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Fri Dec 28 09:19:20 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Fri, 28 Dec 2001 22:19:20 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] FTP problems
In-Reply-To: Message from Bruce Axtens <axtens_@mac.com>
 of "Fri, 28 Dec 2001 16:40:05 +0800." <7DF4D412-FB6E-11D5-949F-0003933D8C18@mac.com>
Message-ID: <200112280919.WAA09230@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <7DF4D412-FB6E-11D5-949F-0003933D8C18@mac.com>, Bruce Axtens writes:
>On Friday, December 28, 2001, at 04:04  PM, Ewen McNeill wrote:
>> Don't use FTP.  Use HTTP.  It's much cleaner.)
>
>Pardon my newbie-ness but, like, how?

HTTP uses a single connection from client->server for all transfers
(originally one per file transfered, but HTTP/1.1 allows more than one
file transfer per connection).  It can be easily proxied/cached, and easily
allowed specifically through a firewall.  All meta information is passed
in a clean, extendable, set of headers on the request and the response.

FTP uses two connections, a control connection and a data connection
(well, one data connection per file transferred).  The control
connection is used to set up the data connections, and no much else.
FTP has two modes: active FTP (the original) where the data connection
goes from sender to receiver (so if the server sends you a file, it
opens a connection back to you), and passive FTP (a later work around)
where the data connection goes from client to server (always).  

FTP picks the port numbers for the data port "at random" (some FTP
clients/servers can be told to be more specific, but in general you
can't assume what the port numbers will be).

So FTP is very hard to firewall.  A firewall at the client end will
generally break active FTP (won't allow the data connection to come
in), unless the firewall specifically knows about FTP and takes special
precautions.  A firewall at the server end will often break active FTP (if
the server isn't allowed to connect back out again), and will generally
break passive FTP as well (since it'll only allow incoming connections
to ports it knows about, and the data connections are chosen "at random").

FTP is also difficult to proxy (at least in the sense of a FTP proxy
that looks like a FTP server on one side and a FTP client on the other), 
since the proxy has to implement pretty much all of the FTP server
behaviour (cf a HTTP proxy which just passes the connections through
with some extra headers).

FTP has no reliable way to return date/time meta information about
files; each FTP client "guesses" this information from directory
listings, after having guessed what the directory listing format is.
HTTP specifically includes this information in its answer.  HTTP has a
"get if modified" request; the equivilent in FTP involves getting a
directory listing, guessing the format, guessing the details of the
file, comparing it with what you have, and hoping for the best.

There's plenty more.  But basically FTP was designed by a bunch of grad
students 20-something years ago making it up as they went along to solve
a much more general problem than was really required, in an environment
security and firewalls weren't an issue.  HTTP was designed more
recently (about 10 years ago), and is much more firewall friendly.

For single file transfers HTTP is more efficient (only one connection
setup); for multiple file transfers FTP doesn't look quite so bad, but
HTTP/1.1 keep-alive connections can give HTTP an edge even there.

Use HTTP.

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

I remember having this same problem when first using Xitami. The solution,

From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)

Subject: [Xitami] FTP problems
References: <200112280919.WAA09230@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>
Message-ID: <3C2D095D.F5DE0408@rci.rutgers.edu>

>Pardon my newbie-ness but, like, how?

Ewen, I think Bruce was asking "How do I use HTTP for FTP-type
stuff?" rather than "How is HTTP better?"

It isn't quite clear what Bruce is doing. But I turn to FTP for
many small chores. My text-editor has a "Save As... FTP" that
opens an FTP server as if it were a local disk (almost), but no
HTTP protocol there. Sucking a LOT of files from one machine to
another (as when moving a site from one host to another) is
natural in a smart FTP client (WS_FTP understands "move directory
structure" as a sequence of basic FTP commands). 

While I'm dimly aware that HTTP can support all this, it isn't so
often done. And I thought Xitami did not natively support HTTP
PUT?

 -PRR

In message <h97r2u4n41i5puutnlc1k4ce7iemq24gnn@4ax.com>, Jon Hinchliffe writes:
>Hopefully this is a simple questions and I recently had to reinstall my
>machine and ever since I haven't be able to get Internet Explorer to find
>my local servers ie http://127.0.0.2/ etc

127.0.0._2_?  That's a fairly unusual address to be using.  Are you sure
you don't mean 127.0.0.1?  You might want to try pinging the IP address
you're trying to use first, to make sure the computer can see it.  As
well as any details from the IE error message (turn off the "friendly"
error messages to get the real deal as to what is going wrong).

Ewen

In message <5ier2uotu7qa5nfdo7vlj2b2hb2fqj2dmn@4ax.com>, Jon Hinchliffe writes:
>On Sat, 29 Dec 2001 23:54:03 +1300, Ewen McNeill <ewen@imatix.com> wrote:
>>In message <h97r2u4n41i5puutnlc1k4ce7iemq24gnn@4ax.com>, Jon Hinchliffe writes:
>>127.0.0._2_?  That's a fairly unusual address to be using.
>
>Well I only use Xitami for testing things offline. I have two websites ie
>Domain names so I set up one on
>
>127.0.0.2 praying.cfg

Well, if it works for you, by all means keep doing so.  Typically only
127.0.0.1 is actually supported as a loop back interface.  And
name-based virtual hosting (rather than IP address based virtual
hosting) is often the way people use to test multiple sites on a single
IP address.

>I solved my problem thanks to your help anyway. Once I turned of the
>(un)helpful messages I got  [useful error message]

:-)  The "friendly" error messages are one of the more annoying features
of IE.  It's a shame they didn't put the friendly message at the top and
then some sort of "technical section" at the bottom of the page with the
real details in it.  This way anyone developing websites/setting up
webservers/whatever has to remember to turn off the "hide error
messages" option (under its other name).

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Dec 29 21:14:09 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 30 Dec 2001 10:14:09 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] devices problem
In-Reply-To: Message from Francis Turner <francis.turner@freesbee.fr>
 of "Sat, 29 Dec 2001 14:41:12 BST." <3C2DC7F8.1000402@freesbee.fr>
Message-ID: <200112292114.KAA30754@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <3C2DC7F8.1000402@freesbee.fr>, Francis Turner writes:
>Jason Ozin at Technica Solutions wrote:
>>Ewen says:
>> > Can anyone else reproduce this issue on another version of Windows?
>>
>>I would remind you that I can produce a similar effect see our previous
>>thread: RE: [Xitami] DoS Bug still in v2.4d9 (W2K service)
>
>I have now just reproduced Jason's bug. http://localhost/lpt1 kills 
>xitami if a printer is installed on win2k

And doesn't if no printer is installed?  (Can someone check this:
temporarily uninstall the printer in Windows, and try again to see if it
locks up.)

I'm wondering if the key difference from the last set of problems is
whether or not there is an actual device (modem, printer, whatever) 
installed on the particular port name in question (aux, lpt, etc).

The fix in Xitami 2.4d9/2.5b4 was to take each filename it was asked to
open, open it, and ask Windows "is this a file?" -- if Windows said
anything other than "yes, it's a normal file", then Xitami closed it
again and backed away quickly (returning 403 etc).  

Possibly this test is either (a) getting an unexpected result when there
is a real device installed, or (b) something about doing the test that
way causes problems when there is a real device installed.

Also, can those who have crashes with "http://localhost/lpt1" please try
"http://localhost/prn" (which ought to be the same device, according to
DOS tradition), and see if it gives the same effect.

Please report:
(a) the exact URL used during testing (including the exact upper/lower 
    case, etc)
(b) the version of Xitami being used (2.4d9, 2.5b5, windows gui, windows
    console, nt service)
(c) the version of Windows you have
(d) what web browser you used (name, and version)
(e) any service packs, patches, etc that you have
(f) what devices you have installed (modem, printer, etc)
(g) what crashes (eg, just xitami so you can kill it off and keep going;
    the OS freezes so you need to ctrl-alt-del and reboot; the OS
    freezes so hard that you can only turn the machine off/hit reset)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sat Dec 29 23:02:42 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 30 Dec 2001 12:02:42 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] devices problem

In message <004401c190ba$20419410$1564a8c0@troy.ozin.foo>, "Jason Ozin at Techni
ca Solutions" writes:
> > Blargh! Same with a NT 4.0 box!!! (at least the /aux does)
> > Haven't tried com1 yet -- not sure if I want to....
>
>Funny I have no problems with aux, just LPT1. What is aux anyway? 

I was going to ask if you had problems with AUX. 

AUX is the "auxillary device", dating _way_ back to the CP/M days.
It's basically another name for one of the COM ports these days --
that people have problems with AUX and COM1 does not surprise me at all.

I suspect that:
- anyone who has a problem with lpt1 will have the problem with prn, 
  and vice versa
- anyone who has a problem with aux will have a problem with com1 (or 
  perhaps one of the other com ports)

(If anyone has problems with only one of prn/lpt1 or only one of
com1/aux please speak up!)

And as mentioned before, I suspect the issue is now restricted to
situations where the device is actually present (eg, a printer
installed).  

If someone who has the problem with prn or lpt1 could try uninstalling
the printer, and see if the problem goes away, and then try installing
the printer again, and see if the problem returns, that would probably
confirm this part of the hypothesis.

The other interesting factor from your detailed post is that it doesn't
happen every time, only when you've hit refresh a lot.  That screams
"race condition" to me -- ie, that it's only when the access happens at
an "inconvenient" time that the problem occurs.

I've got a vague hunch now as to where the race condition might be _if_ the
problem goes away when the printer is uninstalled and comes back when it
is installed.  (Figuring out how to fix it will be a little more tricky,
but I've got one possibility to try there.  Of course the fact that I
can't reproduce this doesn't make it any easier...)

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

Subject: [Xitami] virtual host

On Sat, 2001-12-29 at 14:32, dotcom-fm wrote:
> Hello!
> If any can tell mi how I can set DNS based virtual host on one IP adress? My domain is www.limit.pl, what can I do to set www.sklep.limit.pl (on the same IP)? Of course my server is Xitami!!! (sorry my english)

In the latest beta you can use the virtual host wizard from the front
web page.  You can also do it manually in your config file like this:

[Virtual-hosts]
	www.sklep.limit.pl = "skelp.cfg"


The contents of skelp.cfg would look like this:
[Server]
	webpages = "c:\\Xitami\\skelpwww\\"

This [Server] section tells xitami that when a request for
www.sklep.limit.pl is recieved, the files are located in the director
c:\\Xitami\\skelpwww\\"


The wizard is the easiest way to get this setup though.

-- 
Regards,
Scott Tyson
scott@therubberroom.org
