From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Dec 30 00:53:13 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 30 Dec 2001 13:53:13 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] devices problem
In-Reply-To: Message from "Jason Ozin at Technica Solutions" <jason@tec1.co.uk>
 of "Sun, 30 Dec 2001 00:05:01 -0000." <006401c190c5$a0299000$1564a8c0@troy.ozin.foo>
Message-ID: <200112300053.NAA00928@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <006401c190c5$a0299000$1564a8c0@troy.ozin.foo>, "Jason Ozin at Techni
ca Solutions" writes:
> > I was going to ask if you had problems with AUX.
>
>Ok I've now done the definitive test. I created a new printer (generic text
>only) and told the OS it was on COM1 (it didn't actually exist you
>understand). I then entered www.xxx.com/com1 into Opera and lo and behold it
>crashes. The same for AUX. So that is it I'd say. Your theory is correct.

Okay, it sounds like the fix in 2.4d9/2.5b5 narrows it down to the
situation where:
(a) the device actually exists and is being used (eg, a printer is
    installed); and
(b) the timing of the access is "unlucky"

> > The other interesting factor from your detailed post is that it doesn't
> > happen every time, only when you've hit refresh a lot.  That screams
> > "race condition" to me
>
>Well... yes but don't get too stuck on this as I can make it happen on the
>very first go sometimes as well. I did with the COM1 test above.

_Sometimes_ "first go" is fine -- that can still easily be a race
condition, it's just that the timing happened to be right the first
time.

If it was _always_ first time, then it wouldn't be a race condition
(since it'd be repeatable quite easily), but it doesn't sound like
that's the case here.

The "device problem" handling in Xitami 2.4d9/2.5b5 (same code in both;
testing one version or the other is fine folks -- but no earlier
versions have the fix) works like this:

Try to open the path name given
If it opened:
   Ask Windows "what type of file have I opened?"
   If Windows says "a disk file": it's not a device
   If Windows says anything else: it's probably a device, ignore it
If it did not open:
   Assume that it isn't a device

If the path name is not a device:
   Open the file for reading (to start sending the results out)

The catch is that the file is being opened twice, once to check what
type of file it is, and once to actually access the data.
(Unfortunately we need to do this because only the special Windows API
call will let us ask if it is a device file, but everything else in
Xitami uses the more portable C standard file handles.)

If "something changes" between these two situations, so that the first
open fails, and the second one succeeds, then I think we'll get the
problem we're noticing here (at least if the path name is a device
file).

And my guess is the "something changing" is something like another program
having the device open (blocking us out, so we assume it is not a device)
when we first try to find out if it is a device, and but it has closed it
(freeing up the device) by the time we try to open it again to read from
it.

Unfortunately the Windows API documentation doesn't have much detail
about doing this type of test, or what types of errors we can get back
from the first open attempt, so we're left to guess what might happen.
(It would be _really_ handy for instance if the first open gave us an
error of "someone else is using that device right now" for instance,
then we could know if it was a device even if the open failed.)

I've got a couple of ideas to try, although as I commented, I'm somewhat
hampered by the fact that I can't reproduce the problem...

Ewen

-- 
Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Dec 30 09:13:18 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Paul Reid)
Date: Sun, 30 Dec 2001 04:13:18 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] devices problem
References: <004401c190ba$20419410$1564a8c0@troy.ozin.foo>
Message-ID: <3C2EDAAE.2AF45A71@rci.rutgers.edu>

> What is aux anyway? 

In CP/M (before MS-DOS), the devices were CON, PRN, PUN, and AUX. 

CON was (still is) the CONsole: display and keyboard, teletype or
CRT. 

PRN is a printer, and generally Serial (but not always RS-232!)

PUN is the paper-tape punch, to save data on. (I can't remember
if you read tape on the same port or if there was another, RDR?)

AUX was basically "extra", like spare inputs on the back of a
hi-fi amplifier. Usually AUX pointed to the serial port driver. 

IBM had CP/M in mind when they made the IBM PC. The first O/S for
the PC was that thing Gates bought and modified, which IBM sold
as IBM PC-DOS. But IBM had mapped out multiple serial ports and
adopted a parallel interface for the Epson printer they were
re-badging. So the ports had to have more names to cover all the
new possibilities. LPT1 LPT2 LPT3 (and LPT4 on PS/2 BIOS) denote
the parallel ports. For back-compatability, by default PRN points
to the same routine as LPT1. 

A fully IBM compatible PC has a display much faster than any
serial port, and CON defaults there. However you can re-map CON
to a serial port and there is even a utility to do so. I once had
an Intel-made 286 that would run DOS but was -not- IBM PC
compatible: no internal video. On that beast, CON defaulted to
one of the serial ports and DOS and WordStar ran on a terminal. 

There are a LOT of reserved device names in this tradition.
MS-DOS 2+ has CLOCK (or CLOCK$$). And let us not forget NUL.
Win95/WinNT extend this by giving "LPT1.DOS" a special meaning:
much like "LPT1" but not quite. 

 -PRR

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Sun Dec 30 09:02:17 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Ewen McNeill)
Date: Sun, 30 Dec 2001 22:02:17 +1300
Subject: [Xitami] CGI Perl scripts
In-Reply-To: Message from Bruce <bd4u@earthlink.net>
 of "Sun, 30 Dec 2001 00:36:31 CDT." <jn9t2u0l34luek81hhu1h00somm8okh32h@4ax.com>
Message-ID: <200112300902.WAA01564@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz>

In message <jn9t2u0l34luek81hhu1h00somm8okh32h@4ax.com>, Bruce writes:
>$cgiurl 
>The url portion of the address to the guestbook.pl file The file
>guestbook.pl needs to be placed in your server's cgi-bin and chmoded
>read/execute for users of your httpd. (chmod a+rx) 
>
>to a "guestbook.pl script being used under Xitami?

Put it in Xitami's CGI-BIN directory, make sure you have Perl installed,
and that the Perl executable is on your PATH (eg c:\perl\bin is in your
PATH).  If you're running on Windows then Xitami will treat things in
the cgi-bin directory that have a #! line as their first line that
mentions "perl" in it, as perl programs to run; the chmod is not
necessary under Windows (it's a unix/linux thing).

Ewen

Ewen McNeill, Technical Consultant, iMatix Corporation  www.imatix.com

The easiest way is with windows explorer (and you have all the windows 
explorer functionalities, like drag-and-drop).

1
Start windows explorer

2
in the address bar type ftp://aaa.bbb.ccc
if you don't have an address bar in we, go to View, Toolbars, and click 
address bar

3
now the right part of the screen is the remote location

4
If you have to log in with login and password, click on File, Login...

It's that easy!

I'm not so sure that nothing else is using the device; amongst other
things Windows is able to monitor the paper status of a printer, and I'm
guessing that involves opening the device, querying the status, and
closing the device again.  Providing a window of opportunity for Murphy
(of Murphy's law fame) to sneak in.

Given the way that Xitami works I'd be surprised if it was Xitami itself
that was blocking its own test out -- there's no thread switching
between the test point and the file open point.  But the OS could switch
to another proram/task.

> > I've got a couple of ideas to try, although as I commented, I'm somewhat
> > hampered by the fact that I can't reproduce the problem...
>
>Happy to install debug code on my PC if it helps. I suppose your code
>automatically denying access to known device names is a no no?

We tried that before.  The problem is that there are so many,
undocumented, special ways in which Windows can spot the device name in
a longer path, that it rapidly becomes infeasible to properly check for
known device names without also blocking a whole bunch of filenames
which are otherwise valid.

I'll post something here when I've got a test version with a possible
fix/work around in it.

Ewen

That would be the first line :-)  (Of the perl script.)  It should read
something like:

#! /usr/bin/perl

or similar.  For Xitami the important part is that it contains "perl" in
it.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 31 04:49:49 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Russel Olinger)
Date: Sun, 30 Dec 2001 20:49:49 -0800
Subject: [Xitami] CGI Perl scripts
References: <bd4u@earthlink.net>  of "Sun, 30 Dec 2001 14:00:17 CDT." <qlou2u80essafl9cjt88eov26k7h7igg4b@4ax.com> <200112301946.IAA03955@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz> <notu2uocuop9nmjli39r7hoorvovuhd9n4@4ax.com>
Message-ID: <00c201c191b6$93f3ac20$020aa8c0@Master>

1.  #!  is the first line in your perl script.
2.  C:\perl\bin needs to be in your PATH
3.  all perl scripts need to go in your /xitami/cgi-bin directory (or what
ever directory you have designated to hold your CGI files
4.  The URL alias reference would be: <a
href=/cgi-bin/guestbook.pl>Guestbook</a> OR if you wanted the full path it
would be: <a href=http://208.33.152.220/cgi-bin/guestbook.pl>Guestbook</a>
5.  Your reference below is calling an .html file (guestbook.html), not the
perl .pl file

When calling a CGI file you need to call the script itself, in this case the
perl "guestbook.pl" file.  Xitami allows you to define where you are going
to keep your CGI scripts at.  You only get one root location.  By default it
provides you the /cgi-bin directory but you could modify that to
/my_cgi_files or /perl_scripts or what ever you want, assuming that the
directory EXISTS in c:\xitami\.  So when you are calling CGI files through a
href tag the CGI directory needs to be the first directory in the reference
path: <a href=http://x.x.x.x/cgi-bin/....>click here</a>.  Xitami see's the
/cgi-bin in the URL call and then goes to the /cgi-bin directory to complete
the rest of the URL reference.

valid calls assuming Xitami defaults (/cgi-bin must be at the beginning of
the path):
<a href=/cgi-bin/file.pl>
<a href=http://x.x.x.x/cgi-bin/file.pl>
<a href=/cgi-bin/perlscripts/file.pl> ## /perlscripts is a subdirectory and
it must exist for the URL call to work
<a href=/cgi-bin/blah/blah1/blah2/file.pl>

If Xitami is configured to accept /cgi-bin anywhere in the path:
<a href=/personal/cgi-bin/file.pl>
<a href=http://x.x.x.x/files/yourfiles/cgi-bin/myfiles/perlscripts/file.pl>

hope this helps.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 31 13:17:02 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Bruce)
Date: Mon, 31 Dec 2001 08:17:02 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] CGI Perl scripts
In-Reply-To: <00c201c191b6$93f3ac20$020aa8c0@Master>
References: <bd4u@earthlink.net>  of "Sun, 30 Dec 2001 14:00:17 CDT." <qlou2u80essafl9cjt88eov26k7h7igg4b@4ax.com> <200112301946.IAA03955@pagoda.in.naos.co.nz> <notu2uocuop9nmjli39r7hoorvovuhd9n4@4ax.com> <00c201c191b6$93f3ac20$020aa8c0@Master>
Message-ID: <k1p03u8vued6ut9bu84j2bgdtuh1lg7ke1@4ax.com>

On Sun, 30 Dec 2001 20:49:49 -0800, you wrote:

>1.  #!  is the first line in your perl script.
>2.  C:\perl\bin needs to be in your PATH
>3.  all perl scripts need to go in your /xitami/cgi-bin directory (or what
>ever directory you have designated to hold your CGI files
>4.  The URL alias reference would be: <a
>href=/cgi-bin/guestbook.pl>Guestbook</a> OR if you wanted the full path it
>would be: <a href=http://208.33.152.220/cgi-bin/guestbook.pl>Guestbook</a>
>5.  Your reference below is calling an .html file (guestbook.html), not the
>perl .pl file

   It's supposed to be calling the guestbook.html file from within the
Perl script. I'm guessing that is the reason for the dollar symbol in
front of the URL. I'll give it a try based on what U already told me.
I should be able to muddle through it, based upon what U have
already said. Thanx..

Bruce
 

>
>When calling a CGI file you need to call the script itself, in this case the
>perl "guestbook.pl" file.  Xitami allows you to define where you are going
>to keep your CGI scripts at.  You only get one root location.  By default it
>provides you the /cgi-bin directory but you could modify that to
>/my_cgi_files or /perl_scripts or what ever you want, assuming that the
>directory EXISTS in c:\xitami\.  So when you are calling CGI files through a
>href tag the CGI directory needs to be the first directory in the reference
>path: <a href=http://x.x.x.x/cgi-bin/....>click here</a>.  Xitami see's the
>/cgi-bin in the URL call and then goes to the /cgi-bin directory to complete
>the rest of the URL reference.
>
>valid calls assuming Xitami defaults (/cgi-bin must be at the beginning of
>the path):
><a href=/cgi-bin/file.pl>
><a href=http://x.x.x.x/cgi-bin/file.pl>
><a href=/cgi-bin/perlscripts/file.pl> ## /perlscripts is a subdirectory and
>it must exist for the URL call to work
><a href=/cgi-bin/blah/blah1/blah2/file.pl>
>
>If Xitami is configured to accept /cgi-bin anywhere in the path:
><a href=/personal/cgi-bin/file.pl>
><a href=http://x.x.x.x/files/yourfiles/cgi-bin/myfiles/perlscripts/file.pl>
>
>hope this helps.

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 31 14:13:54 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Jim Mooney)
Date: Mon, 31 Dec 2001 09:13:54 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] CGI vs PHP
Message-ID: <20011231.091354.-472405.4.greenalt@juno.com>

I've been fighting CGI and it's awful permissions for so long I've
decided to move to PHP. The latest version of PHP integrates
automatically with the Xitami server so you can learn it very easily. Of
course, the one problem is there is still a dearth of good PHP as opposed
to free perl scripts, for things like bulletin boards or group event
calendars, that are the equal of the ones in Perl at Matt's Script
Archive. I  like Perl but I really get tired setting endless permissions
in the cgi-bin.

Anyone know where I might find a good bbs or calendar in PHP?

And speaking of permissions, I was thinking of getting cable so I'd have
a fixed IP and setting up FTP (which I finally figured out).  But just
how secure is the Xitami FTP? It will be open to the world, so I assume
it's nearly impossible for hackers to break out of so they can go ravage
my disk.

Oy, now I've got to learn server security. PHP today, security tomorrow.
It never ends on the web ;')

Happy New Year, by the way.

Yours,

Jim Mooney, webmaster
www.arizonademocracy.com    www.insurancejustice.com

Hello Folks,

Why is it that the "\n"  and other escape characters in my Perl script are =
not being recognized in the IOExplorer browser?? I start the html code =
with the prescribed  .....print "Content-type: text/html\n\n";..... I'm =
running Win NT 4.0 and perl5 and IOExplorer 5.5.

By the way, after much pain and suffering, I discovered from this Q&A list =
that I had to include the ".pl=3Dapplication/x-http-perl" statement in the =
Mime section and "pl=3DC:\perlpath\perl.exe" in the Filter section of the =
Defaults.cfg file in order to get my NT 4.0 to execute the Perl5 script.=20=

Thanks for that.

Subject: [Xitami] setting up to receive FTP - basic question
Message-ID: <002d01c1920b$c0f40e40$91220718@omhan1.ne.home.com>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_002A_01C191D9.761E1BE0
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="iso-8859-1"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: quoted-printable

Default will be port 21 and your ISP (must allow this on port 21)
The default port address of 21 can be changed using the portbase=3D
in the [Server] section of defaults.cfg if needed. =20

In the defaults.cfg file:   (this is the minimum requirement)
[FTP]
enabled=3D1                        #enable ftp
user-file=3Dftpdirs.aut        #point to password/authorization file

In the ftpdirs.aut file:
[MyFtp]                                    #folder name
user1=3Dpassword1              #user1 password is password1
users2=3Dpassword2            #user2 password is password2



------=_NextPart_000_002A_01C191D9.761E1BE0

From xitami@lists.xitami.org  Mon Dec 31 15:35:28 2001
From: xitami@lists.xitami.org (Frank Harrell)
Date: Mon, 31 Dec 2001 10:35:28 -0500
Subject: [Xitami] Reasigned ports
In-Reply-To: <000801c1920e$1556ebe0$91220718@omhan1.ne.home.com>
Message-ID: <001301c19210$c623c6d0$6500a8c0@COWBOY>

This is a multi-part message in MIME format.

------=_NextPart_000_0014_01C191E6.DD4DBED0
Content-Type: text/plain;
	charset="us-ascii"
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit

General comment on ftp through cable modems. 
 
My ISP was blocking port 80 but not 21, so I had to use a different www
port (I ended up using 443, ssl port, which got around problems with
some firewalls [a friend's at work] which was blocking unusual ports to
unknown ip addresses)
 
The problem was that Xitami would accept the FTP connection and login on
port "which ever" (other than 21), but when my ftp client asked for a
"list" there was either no response from Xitami, or for some reason my
Linksys cable router, or the cable company was blocking the return list.
I got around it by disabling Xitami's FTP and used another FTP program.
 
Frank Harrell
http://CowboyFrank.net  http://asgra.org
http://www.CowboyFrank.dns2go.com 

 
Default will be port 21 and your ISP (must allow this on port 21.)
The default port address of 21 can be changed using the portbase=
in the [Server] section of defaults.cfg if needed. 

In the defaults.cfg file:   (this is the minimum requirement)
[FTP]
enabled=1                        #enable ftp
user-file=ftpdirs.aut        #point to password/authorization file

In the ftpdirs.aut file:
[MyFtp]                                    #folder name
user1=password1              #user1 password is password1
users2=password2            #user2 password is password2
